<Author>genluxx
<Content>Overall a fun stay if you'd like to be right in the action in tourist central I was in town for business. This was a good place to stay if you want to be right in the middle of the action on Hollywood Boulevard, and by action I mean being able to step outside your hotel and be accosted by Daffy Duck or Spiderman or Pocahontas etc. and have shops right at your door. The hotel is opposite The Chinese Theatre so also puts you somewhere easily reminiscable when watching films as you'll frequently see both the hotel and vicinity on tv and in films.There are a lot of bands and celebrities who stay here so this is another level of action that you may seek out.After getting the chance to drive around lots and see different areas I reckon next time I'll probably rent an apartment by the beach, I tend to prefer more low key quiet chilled places with walking potential, and if this strikes a similar chord this hotel may not be for you.Anyway, the hotel itself was made up of a gorgeous exterior and the same if somewhat dark interior, something I've noticed popular in celebrity haunts, 'all the better not to see you with my dear'.The pool is legendary, the rooms okay. Clean a modern take on the 70's but as they are somewhat small and as the mattress sat in the middle of a larger wooden platform I kept bashing my shins on the corners every time I would walk around it- I still have the scars, so this was somewhat annoying.Good desk, smallish window, dark bathroom with not much light, but all in all it was okay.Meals there very pricey, breakfast, oatmeal fruit and tea plus tip set me back over $45. I couldn't relax very well in the rooms though, and I still don't really know why, there was nothing really wrong with it, and a great walk in closet if you're staying there for a while as I was.Some say the hotel is haunted. Who knows.

<Author>MidwestBizzyTraveler
<Content>Disappointed w/ the Roosevelt I was looking forward to my stay at the Roosevelt for a business conference I was attending. The location on Hollywood Blvd., is ideal, with plenty going on around the hotel.The room they initially gave me had an interesting style -- an urban, efficiency apartment feel to it, as I walked through (intentionally) dimly lit hallways with carpeting that mimmicked a brick road. The room had a brick wall interior (still dimly lit-- by design), hardwood floors, and a pavement like (concrete?) floor in the bathroom. The problem was---------- the noise. There wasn't necessarily that much noise, but, because of the (extremely) poor soundproofing of the rooms, ... you could hear very clearly every detail of the conversations in the rooms next to you. It was as if you were sharing a cabin with people you didn't know. When I called the front desk, to ask to have my room changed... they 'played' naive about it, but, I sensed this was a common complaint with guests, in that they quickly ended the charade, and gave me a more conventional room in a different section of the building.That room was indeed quieter, but very, very small. Personally, I'm alright with that.When I opened the door, and walked into the new room, there were two staff members (not housecleaning) that had shocked looks on their faces (guilty looks). They immediately hung up the room phone, and bolted out of my room. I was kind of ticked, and called to make sure there were no charges against my room bill.Because there was limited shelf space and closet space, the housekeeping crew accidently knocked my shaving kit into the toilet when they were cleaning. Rather than fess up to it, they quietyly put it back in it's original location. That evening, when I got back to the room, I reached in, and noticed the thing was saturated with all of my toiletries wet., and items saturated.There was construction going on on the (street) lobby level, so guests needed to take the (only one operating) elevator down to the ground level, and hike back up a set steps to get outside.I know each of these issues sound minor and random, but, my general feeling is that for the price they charge per room, you should expect good customer service and attention to details. At a minimum, a reasonably quiet room would seem like a fair expectation.I wouldn't recommend the Roosevelt... not for the prices they charge. I'm probably going to try the Renaissance the next time I'm in the area. I don't expect everything to be perfect.. I just want a clean and quiet room to stay in, with minimal interruptions. I did not get that.  
<Date>Nov 20, 2008

A movie was being filmed one day of our stay with an enormous amount of equipment but this did not affect us at all. Concierge (Lauren I think) was helpful in organising Limo and with any questions we had.Lobby near main entrance is really old world Hollywood and just beautiful, yes it is dark but that is part of its charm.Location can't be beat right on Hollywood Blvd across from Graumans . Felt safe in this area at night as long as you don't go more than about 5 blocks down. Although my children didn't worry at all and even walked to Sunset at night.Probably not for young children or budget conscious but we loved it!

<Author>Sequin-Sue
<Content>Good hotel, great location We are a couple in our twenties and were pleased with our choice of the Hollywood Roosevelt for a two-night visit. The location is perfect for exploring Hollywood as it's right opposite the Chinese Theatre.The rooms are very small, but nicely done. For a two night visit the room size wasn't a problem, but it might be an issue if you're planning a longer visit. The bathroom was lovely too with a good supply of products by 'Fresh'.The hotel itself is very dark, but that's part of its ambience. The reception was lovely and the concierge very helpful. We asked the concierge to book us tickets to The Police who were playing at the Bowl that evening - she sorted it all out for us while we went out sightseeing and our booking confirmation was under our door when we got in (although she did spend slighty more than we'd agreed).On our first evening at the hotel there was a pool party which looked fun, but a bit overwhelming after a long day travelling - it was packed full of local rich kids, with music from a live DJ. The pool area is lovely during the day, unfortunately we didn't have enough time to make the most of it.We ate in the restaurant once and found the service very impressive. The food was lovely although there was not a great choice for my boyfriend who is vegetarian. The breakfast place within the hotel is very good too. During our stay there was a limited lift service which was annoying as it meant a long wait each time, but I'm sure that was just temporary.Despite the hotel being rather pricey, its a great place to stay to be in the heart of things.

<Author>Captain_Weasel
<Content>This is LA! Just what I thought LA would be like. This is a great looking hotel in a great location. Extremely friendly staff. The concierge was a bit too cool for school but helpful to an extent.Hire car was dealt with very well by reception, and free internet in the foyer made getting local info very easy.The room was nice. Not as big as a lot of American hotels but comfy. We only stayed for two nights and as our room was on the third floor on the same level as the flat roof, we were disturbed on both nights by people drinking on the roof until early in the morning. On the second night, a lady actually managed to enter our room! As easy going young guys this was not a major problem, but I can imagine other people having a big problem with this! Ask not to stay near the flat roof!The pool bar area was absolutely great though, and I think my favourite bar in Hollywood. Full of great looking people, great music, all set against a lit pool beneath the hotel sign. Looked very nice. Just sad I didn't drink there every night.Overall, a very nice hotel exlcuding the disturbances, very friendly beautiful smiley faces everywhere and a great spot to explore Hollywood and Beverly Hills.

<Author>tellsitlikeitisSpain
<Content>Big let Down We arrived at the Hollywood Roosevelt as a newley wed couple after a four and a half hour journey from the beautiful friendly Ritz Carlton hotel at Lake Las Vegas. We walked into the hotel reception feeling like the Beverly Hillbillies, the staff at reception were cold and unfriendly although the receptionist did give us and upgrade to a cabana (Which he said was overlooking the gardens! and was really overlooking a multistorey carpark with a vine growing up the side of it)  The guy who took our bags to the room was friendly he gave us the ins and outs of the place. The hallways were dark, very dark, the cabana room was dark, not as chic as it looks on the website, even with the lights on you need a torch to see in your suitcase. The bathroom was about the same size as the wardrobe and the floor of the room wasnt very clean. All the furniture just looked cheap and tacky not great for the price! We ventured off for a drink (out of the hotel) and luckily we met a nice couple who was also staying in the Roosevelt, after a few drinks we all decided to head back to the Roosevelt and keep on drinking at the Tropicana bar which is at the poolside at the Roosevelt, I had this idea that it would be full of Hollywood glamour and lots of beautiful people but it wasn't. Everyone was dressed casually, very arrogant, rude and pretentious. The hotel was overrun with teenaged kids spending daddy's money.  We were made to feel like intruders everytime we wanted to go to our room as the tropicana security staff would stop us and ask us where we were going and check us off their list, even if you had a bottle of water you were asked to get rid of it (BUT IM JUST GOING TO MY ROOM FOR GODS SAKE!) Don't even bother to ask any of the staff about the history of the hotel, because they don't know. Just read it up before you go and educate them while your there. Also don't bother saying hello or smiling at the staff because they just look at you like your off your trolley.The room was noisey all night long, the walls must be paper thin. Loud music, car alarms, talking from the rooms nearby, dont even get me started on the airconditioning unit! Honestly I thought this hotel was going to be chic, sexy elegent, classy, brimming with Hollywood history and Glamour and it was totally the opposite, which is a big shame. The owners of the hotel seriously need to reconsider who they are contracting the leases of the bars to as they are making this hotel a very uncomfortable place to stay. This hotel could be a magic piece of old Hollywood if it was just managed properly. We left after two nights and I couldnt believe that while we were waiting for the car to be brought round for us to leave, the car valet guy told us which room Marilyn Monroe had lived in for two years and it was the room right across from ours. I'd asked the staff several times and no-one knew. I couldnt believe it i had walked past the room several times and the door had been open and I didnt get a proper look. :( Over all a complete let down.

<Author>MaYBaBeOSU13
<Content>Classic Experience! The Roosevelt Hollywood is a beautiful place to stay, especially if you want to experience the history of it. Marilyn Monroe used to live there in one of the suites above the pool, and she also had her first modeling job at the pool. Many of the old moviestars used to hang out at the hotel for drinks, and it still has that classy feel. The first Academy Awards was also held in one of the meeting rooms there.Rooms: The first night we stayed in the Cabana suite, which was amazing inside. It overlooks the pool, which as other reviews mentioned, does turn into a hotspot at night with fun music and a young crowd. The other nights we stayed in a standard room. It was very nice as well. Soft feather comforter! The only downside is that only the suite had bathroom counter space, so as a girl, it was hard to get ready with just a sink.Pool: The pool is one of the most popular, if not THE most popular, hotel pool in Hollywood. It's surrounded by 50s style suites, pretty palm trees, has wonderful soft lounge chairs/beds, as well as wait staff for food and drinks. The only reason I did not give this hotel a 5 star is because of some rude staff (not all of them, just some).There is a club called Teddy's that very popular, but it turns into a guest list only after 10 or 10:30. It is not owned by the hotel, so that's why people can't just get in even if they're staying at the hotel. Most bars/clubs at night are guest list only so you have to call during the day to get on the list or go early unless you're with all girls.Overall, this hotel is worth the stay just to experience both old and new Hollywood, and it's so close to everything else in LA. 15 min. from the beach, Beverly Hills, etc. The Kodak Theater with all of the famous gold stars and handprints is across the street. You can also see the Hollywood white letters too. The valet service is very friendly and helpful!

<Author>heaven911
<Content>Pretty Good - But Pool Turns into Club Scene at Night I just returned from a 10 day stay at The Roosevelt. I'd heard good reviews from friends but was a little disappointed. I stayed in a regular room with 2 beds overlooking the roof (had a lovely view of the air conditioners). PROS:Bed was very nice -- soft white down comforter and pillows.Front desk and valet staff were very friendly and helpful.Location is great. Restaurants, food and walk of fame etc very close. There is a Longs a block away where you can buy anything you could ever possibly need.CONS:There is a coffee machine in the room but you have to pay 3.50 for the coffee in the mini bar. I've traveled all over the world and don't recall ever seeing that before, is it just me or is that a little ridiculous?Closet was dark due to the dark paint and lack of lighting. Water leaks out the side of the shower so you're guaranteed a pool of water under the sink after every shower.Overall it was a good experience but there is one thing I do want to mention. The pool turns into a club at night and can be a rather nice place to hang out - if you can get past the bouncers. I had no trouble getting in but some of my co-workers did. Despite being guests they were told they needed to be with girls and on another occasion they were told they needed to go change their clothes. Being a hotel guest doesn't guarantee entry or that they'll treat you with respect. So, if you're not in the mood for a club scene, as soon as they put up the velvet ropes avoid the pool.

<Content>All around nice hotel. My boyfriend and I recently stayed at this hotel for our first trip to L.A. The hotel itself is very nice but dark everywhere. Our room was vey modern and decorated nice however the rooms are Very Very small!! Bathrooms are tiny!!!!!! We found the bed too small and uncomfortable, very loud airconditioning fan that you can not turn off, I am not a light sleeper but it kept me awake - on the second night at around 3am I asked at the check in desk if they could get someone to come and turn it off. Very surprised that by the time i had returned to the room this had been done and an engineer had come to turn it off. However on return to the room the next day it had been turned back on again!!! Rooms werent overly clean and hotel in general very dark dingy and noisy. We didnt get to the pool or the restaurants.Valet staff helpfull pleasant and overall appeared to be nice people. Shame about the rest of the staff.Also be aware that when you check in they charge your credit card $150 for every night you will be there as incidentals then refund it on check out. We were not informed of this on check in and had tried to use our card whilst we were out and had it declined - took about 3 dys after checkout to have the money returned to our card.

<Author>Penelope_Keith
<Content>Hollywood Roosevelt My friend and I stayed at the Hollywood Roosevelt for 3 nights from 4 Aug 08. The location was really good for tourists without a car. Across the road was the Hollywood  Highland Center which had numerous shops and eateries. There was also a pharmacy and supermarket nearby.The hotel looks very luxurious inside as you would expect for the price (about $279/night + tax). We didn't get to the pool or Tropicana bar. There is a restaurant within the hotel for those wanting more than fast food.The room was fine, but wouldn't want to be any smaller. It had a fridge and well stocked mini bar, which we didn't take advantage of.The bathroom was a bit of a disappointment. It was small, but doable in terms of space, except for the toilet being too close to the wall. This is one of my pet hates along with a passive air vent rather than an electric exhaust fan, so the bathroom fogged up quickly and took a while to de-fog. They provided nice toiletries.Our room looked out over.. a rooftop. Our room also backed on to the elevators and so there was some noise at night when they were used. Other rooms shouldn't have had this issue.If you need a taxi, the valet parking guys have taxis on standby that they call over immediately.I believe they had two standing only internet terminals for guests.Overall, the hotel was fine, but bathroom let it down. Location was good.

<Author>LittleMissShiny
<Content>Lost Soul My family and I visisted this hotel six years ago and we were disappointed with the changes when we re-visited in June.The historical lobby is no longer the main entrance and is very dingy and dark. All the historical material and the piano has been removed so it feels soulless.When private parties are held at the hotel, residents are not allowed to use the Hollywood Boulevard entrance, the lobby, the pool or the gym.When we arrived after being up for nearly 24 hours, we had to prove we had a reservation before we were allowed on to the premises. They seemed to be more interested in the celebrities than their hotel guests.Non residents are allowed to use the pool which regularly means there is no where to sit. Also, you are not allowed to eat your own food there as they have a small restaurant which serves food and drink.The gift shop appears to be stocked with fashionable items which are very expensive and are not for the regular tourist.The hotel prides itself on the fact that the Oscars were held there but you would be hard pressed to see any evidence.The air conditioning was very loud and would keep light sleepers awake.On a positive note, the room we stayed in was very clean and the position of the hotel is excellent for visiting the area.

The hotel staff was nice, but come to Hollywood with a plan of what you want to see and do, don't count on them to help with planning. I loved this hotel and area, and can't wait to go back!! Also, there is a restaurant called 25degrees and they have the best burgers!!

<Author>vanessam
<Content>Loved the Ambience We wanted to stay in a hotel that had some character this hotel oozes glamour and is very elegant. We were not disappointed with our choice. We did book a supieror room and on checking in found the reception and bell staff very friendly and helpful. We were upgraded to a poolside cabana room and we accepted even though we were fully aware of the reviews mentioning the noise problem from Tropicana Bar. We found the music was louder during the day then late at night, however we were at the Tropicana bar until 12.30am anyway. I have read alot of the comments that the hotel is dark this is true however I found it to be in keeping with the hotels atmosphere and creates the elegant ambience expecially in the main lobby and bar areas. We had pre dinner drinks in Teddys/Library bar great atmosphere and dined in Dakota for dinner the service and food was great. The hotel is very central to everything in Hollywood and there was even a movie premier across the road. You will also find that most of the tour groups leave from the Kodak Theatre across the road. The only down side was that the concierge didn't book our airport shuttle after she said she would and we were lucky enough to get one at the last minute (1 hour before we had be picked up).

<Author>thepurple_monkey
<Content>Great hotel - not for families My brother and I stayed at the Roosevelt from April 9 to 13, 2008. Front desk staff was extremely helpful and polite, as was the concierge, both giving us great dining and partying suggestions, and helping get us in to the hottest places in Hollywood.The room was average, nothing to brag about. We had room 510 (2 double beds). It is true that the bathrooms are a bit tight, and the furniture, although it looks modern (due to dark colors) is a bit old and chipped here and there, but I really can't complain that much. If you're staying at the Roosevelt, it's not cause you're going to be in the room much!!!25 degrees and Dakota are both excellent restaurants. I had one of the best steaks of my life at Dakota (and I've eaten alot of steak all over the US and Canada!!!). Tropicana bar is the place to be in Hollywood after dark, as well as happy hour! (don't even bother going to clubs, Tropicana and the lobby bar is where the action is at!!)The hotel is great for the 21-35 crowd, but I don't see it being that great for families (it's kind of dark, literally not much lighting, everywhere) and lots socializing... Overall, great place to stay, would stay again, but Hollywood and L.A. in general is not what we expected. If you go to California, go to San Diego, Santa Monica, Pasadena, Venice beach and Disney land (all beautiful), and try to spend as little time in hollywood or L.A. as possible (beverly hills is the only thing to see there, and that's a half day situation, extensive shopping included!)

<Author>juckett
<Content>Unique experience If you want a brand new hotel with all the amenities and clean lines of a new hotel, this place is not for you. However, if you want a unique experience at an old Hollywood hotel, then book it. While some of the rooms are very small, and they don't come cheaply, the service that we received from the concierges (Lauren and Adam), bellhops, and parking attendants was outstanding. They exerted a fair amount of effort to ensure that our trip was pleasant and our needs were taken care of. The lobby of the Roosevelt is one of the prettiest lobbies (again old) of any hotel I have stayed. I found the 25 degrees restaurant (open 24 hours) to be above average - although their menu was a little oddly set up. The room was not spectacular, but I believe that is what you get with an older hotel. The bed was relatively comfortable and bathroom was small (hard for the fatter than average American) and had a shower drain that drained very slowly. However, the location was amazing, convenient to many things (we drove to Beverly Hills in 15 minutes, West Hollywood in 10, Hollywood sign in 5, Warner Studios in 15-20, and out to Santa Monica in 30-35 - all in LA traffic). I would recommend as long as you are okay with older hotels.

<Author>ValerieMow
<Content>Great Location!!! We arrived in Hollywood and were quite overwelmed by the fast pace of the place and were even more shocked by the valet parking at the Roosevelt hotel - it was very expensive. We were a bit early for check in but there were no problems. The room itself was a bit small but had everything in it.The decor of the hotel was lovely and the lobby was out of this world. There were quite a few weddings taking place in it while we were there.The pool was a different story!! Impossible to get a bed and at times was closed without any notice!! The one time that we did actually get to the pool (a sunday) it was terrible!! There seemed to be an influx of young, hip, toned and very loud people who had stayed in the hotel for the weekend. We felt totally out of place with our books while quietly sunbathing!! The norm appeared to be very much loudness, drinking and dancing by the pool!! Mann's Chinese Theatre and the Kodak Theatre are across the road and all the other main attractions such as Universal Studios and Venice Beach are all very close by. Great hotel for celeb spotting - Rushour 3 premiered across the road!The staff were also very friendly and it was nice to say we stayed in the Roosevelt hotel but I don't think we would stay in it again.

<Author>LondonJetSetters
<Content>Could use some sprucing up! The Roosevelt Hotel is a totally FINE experience for someone who wants to be out and about and enjoy LA. The price was reasonable enough, the rooms were fine, and there is a fun scene at the pool bar. As per other reviewers, the parking is expensive-- it is actually $28/day and we imagined we would just use public parking but all the parking nearby is closed overnight, so this is impossible. We looked at 5 rooms before we found one that was a reasonable size (and we were not in the cheapest room category) and then, picked one that smelled of smoke, because at least we could walk around it. The rooms were all quite worn-- chipped furniture, chipped bathtubs, but it did seem clean enough. All in all, I don't feel the need to COMPLAIN about the hotel, but I wouldn't give it a rave either. It is a good place to stay if you are in LA to have fun-- out and about during the day and on the town at night...

<Author>BobAdams111
<Content>Great Hotel! I stayed at this hotel for two nights while on business in Hollywood, CA and I really enjoyed my stay. This is a great hotel (high 4 stars) and it is very different from most luxury hotels I've stayed at. The design is modern and chique and this fits in well with Hollywood Blvd. Overall, I enjoyed the atmosphere, the cleanliness of the hotel, the quality of the accommodations, and the convenience to where I needed to be. Also, it was nice meeting celebrities by the pool at night!Here are some things I did not like:1. No Heat. There was AC only. At night, temperatures in LA dropped to 30 degrees and heat was needed.2. There is only a fitted sheet and a comforter on the bed. There is no sheets between the fitted sheet and the comforter. You use the comforter as your only blanket. While the front desk assured me they clean each comforter every night, I like a sheet and I found this unusual.3. The bathroom was dimly lit.4. The lobby is a historic and well decorated lobby. Yet, it has the atmosphere of a night club. There is virtually no light except for candles and I thought this was a shame. It's an impressive lobby and I would have liked to enjoy this room.

<Author>fly4fun2
<Content>Interesting I'd booked a deluxe room as I was hoping this would be away from the noise. I was offered an upgrade to a suite for $50. Great I thought until he told me it was $50 a night. I was there for 3 and we took the upgrade as we'd just stayed at the best hotel ever in Vegas (Thanks Tripadvisor!). This is an old hotel that has had a facelift (or two, this being LA and all!!) . The room was probably two rooms in a past life, but it was worth the extra money to have all that space. Half of it may have been too small. We had a great view of the Chinese Theatre and Hollywood sign. We were on the 9th floor.It was too cold and grey to use the pool, and we only saw it on our last day anyway. Looks like a great place to spend time. The lobby bar is pricey, but it is classy and funky. We could hear it from our room at night, the bass throbbing through the building. Thankfully earplugs and sleeping tablets helped hide that! As a first time tourist to LA its hard to find somewhere central to stay in a town that has no heart. For a location though this wasn't bad as the boulovard wasn't too unsafe at night, given the crowds outside. Loads of safe places in the Hollywood and Highlands complex next to the Kodak Theatre as well as the ones in the hotel - Note 21 degrees burgers - order one mixed portion of onion rings and fries for two as it's plenty! This isn't a cookie cutter hotel, so expect it to have a bit of charm and character for it's age. It's a funky place to stay and if you are looking for the different, then come here. If you want a standard type of hotel, then go to a Hitlon or Marriot etc.

<Author>bjpeart
<Content>Cool, Cool, Cool - a great place to stay. As a traveling musician, I stayed at the Roosevelt while playing a show in Hollywood. My wife and I were issued a beautiful corner room overlooking the famed Hollywood sign and the Chinese theater out one window, and and the walk of fame, a great view of the city and other landmarks out the other window. The room was very modern, but homey, with a flat screen television, high speed internet, a very comfortable bed, and a great bathroom. Lots of storage space was nice as well.As great as the accomodations were, the service is what really knocked me off my feet. Everyone on staff, from the waiters and waitresses, the front desk personel, the cleaning staff, and even the valet staff were very courteous, friendly and - gasp - helpful! Much different from what I expected in Los Angeles of all places.(If you're into it, we also saw a number of Celebrities while staying at the Roosevelt. Not necessarily my thing, but still kinda cool.....) The restaurants in the hotel were top notch as well, especially 25 degrees, where I had one of the best gourment hamburgers I've ever tasted (at 4am in the morning, nonetheless). If you're in town to see the sights of Hollywood, there's probably no better place to stay. The price might be a deterrent to some, but if you want to truly experience the area, this is worth every penny.

<Content>Loved the Roosevelt We recently stayed at the Hollywood Roosevelt Hotel for a short girls weekend to L.A (my friends and I are 30). We would stay at the Roosevelt again if we were ever in the area. Bed was very comfortable.

<Author>jsdCalifornia
<Content>Pleasant Surprise My daughter and I took a quick one-night trip to LA to see Wicked. Since we were only staying for one night, I used Priceline which came up with the Roosevelt Hotel. After reading many reviews of this hotel, I must admit that I had low expectations. The review comments that most stood out were small dark rooms and rude staff. I must say that my experience was very different. We arrived at noon, before check-in, but were treated very politely at the front desk. They advised that only one room with two beds was available, it was 'nice' and on the 8th floor, but was handicapped accessible. We decided to take the room and it was lovely. It had views of the Hollywood sign, the Chinese Theater and the Magic Castle. It was also quite large and bright. When we got to the room, we noticed that the shower had been used, a bathmat was on the floor and a towel was in the sink. I called housekeeping, they were very apologetic, and said it would be taken care of. We were not really bothered by this, and assume the room was cleaned while the previous guest was at the pool. (This happened to us once when we were at the pool and our room was cleaned early - we did tell the front desk upon checkout, but have no idea if they relayed the message to the housekeeping staff.) We left to do some shopping and have lunch, when we returned the room had been re-cleaned. The poolside bar/restaurant was really nice and since it was extremely hot, the staff was very obliging and moved an umbrella over to our table to provide shade. About the only negative comment is that there are no ice machines, and ice must be ordered from room service. After returning from the theater we really wanted ice water, so I called room service to ask how long it would take. I was assured that it would only be about 10 minutes, but after 45 minutes, we gave up and went to sleep. Next time, I would just go to the 24 hr. restaurant and ask for a glass of ice. Breakfast in the restaurant was also very good. Other comments on this site have mentioned that the pool area and bar are sometimes closed for private parties, but since we had no intention of using the pool at night, or going to the bar (since my daughter is too young) it was not an issue. All in all, it was a very wonderful experience and I would recommend this hotel.  
<Date>Sep 10, 2007

<Author>havanahipster
<Content>Chic but really loud at night This is a very chic hotel (consistent with the Thompson hotel properties in NYC). The rooms are elegantly understated with hardwood floors, platform bed, and miminalist design. I had a cabana room that overlooked the pool. During the day you will see many locals hanging around the pool or a production company shooting a commercial. Celebrity sightings are common here.At night, this pool area is quite the party scene. If you have any plans to sleep at night, don't stay at this hotel. Seriously. I am a heavy sleeper, but the noise was so loud, and it went on until at least 1 am, and this was on a Wednesday night!! So, if you are here on a business trip and need to be awake for an early morning meeting or to get to the airport, stay somewhere else.

<Author>tim1966
<Content>A great one night stay. I was very concerned after booking this hotel through Priceline that I had made a big mistake! Small rooms, poor service and noise seemed to be the general feeling coming from many reviewers. I was considering walking away from the reservation but in the end decided to 'chance' it.I was so glad I did, check in staff where friendly and efficient and after discovering it was our first time staying at the Roosevelt spent a good few minutes going through all the facilities that were on offer.After expecting a tiny room I was delighted with the corner room I was given on the 7th floor. It had two twin beds with very comfortable linens, very effective air conditioning and a great view towards downtown LA. The bathroom was not huge, however, it was fine for 1 night, there was also plenty of storage space in the closets in the small corridor as you entered the room. The mini-bar was well stocked however, the prices were extremely expensive. It was good to see that it wasn't one of those mini-bars were the slightest movement of an item causes a charge to be made. This meant it was possible to store a few beers and other items in there with no problem. The historic lobby is dark as had been stated previously however, it was like a calm oasis after battling through the heat and crowds on Hollywood Boulevard. It was also a great place to enjoy a few drinks before retiring as the pool bar is closed on Sunday evenings.I only had a brief opportunity to see the pool area on the Sunday afternoon of my stay, however it definitely had a 'vibe' about the place and was certainly full of 'beautiful' people. All in all it was a great 'Hollywood' experience for the end of my vacation and if people get the same treatment as I and my partner did I can whole-heartedly recommend this hotel.

<Author>PegLar
<Content>Historic Hollywood Meets Luxurious Fun Even if you live in Southern California, you shouldn't miss a chance to stay at the Hollywood Roosevelt Hotel. The ambiance of the hotel makes the guest feel like a star - if only for the night. Every detail in our renovated room was perfect - the modern but comfortable furniture, the marble-clad bath, the view of Grauman's Chinese Theatre across the street. The room included great (and stylish) lighting for working at the desk or reading in bed. I loved the photos of movie stars lining the hallways and the sense of historic Hollywood. If only the walls could talk! The interiors of the hotel public rooms are amazing. You can sit in the library bar and marvel at all the intricate details in the woodwork, textiles and tile. It's a marvelous mix of different styles that echo the historic past and current scene that is the Hollywood. Best of all, and in spite of it's celebrity power, it isn't fussy. Check-in was professional yet friendly. You'll wait for your car at valet parking just like any popular spot but this doesn't diminish the fun of staying here. You are so distracted by the lux autos and the people driving them that it doesn't matter. Highly recommended for a true taste of Hollywood glamour!

<Author>fun4uinbshore
<Content>Great Hotel and Great Experience This is the place to stay in Hollywood. I read some scathing reviews and was prepared to walk if all was not in order (actually had a back up reservation across the street). We booked a pool view cabana room. We got a very nice sized room with an awesome king bed with great sheets. The room was dark but not uncomfortably so. The view of the pool and immediate access to the pool was nice. I can't imagine being in the tower rooms since so much of this hotel revolves around the pool and the Tropicana.  When we arrived the valet was courteous, check in efficient and the bellman superb giving us some hints. This was my girlfriend's birthday and all was in order. Oh yeah, we are not in our 20's, but late 40's, and we did not feel out of place at the pool. We made contact with a pool attendant Greg immediately, and made arrangements for specific lounge chairs by Hollywood's most popular pool. It helps if you are wiling to tip to get prime real estate by the pool, and want to sleep in. While the drinks and pool snacks are a little pricey hey it's a vacation relax and go with it. The pool becomes a nightclub at night with a line, but as a cabana guest you have access with no questions. it can be loud until about 1:20am, so be warned. Well worth stopping here for a drink on the way to your room The Library lobby bar is beautiful and serves up drinks in a more sedate atmosphere. While there you really should try Dakota for a high end steak dining experience. Excellent service and corkage for $20.00. Also try the killer hamburger and breakfast bar open 24 hours it is called 25 Degrees. The hotel walking distance to all the great places in Hollywood. We did the Magic Castle and Pantages (Wicked). The only bummer is we did not have time for Musso and Frank Grill. I am already thinking about booking another weekend here.

<Author>Elysium73
<Content>Awful, awful, awful!! Stayed for 3 nights - final stop on a great honeymoon, on the way back to the UK from Fiji. Chose the hotel because we were expecting a little bit of Old-Hollywood chic, and because of it's central location.Room was tiny by American standards. Particularly the bathroom which more closely resembled one from a Japanese capsule hotel. Room was decorated with a frankly disgusting large canvas photograph. Walls were paper-thin (we could hear conversations in the room next door), bed and pillows weren't particularly comfortable (and my partner swears there was bed bugs due to the mysterious bites she kept waking up with), though the TV had a good selection of channels.The hotel istself is so dark and dingy. Even with blazing sunshine outside, it's very gloomy in the lobby. It's also very noisy and busy; there always seemed to be something happening. The doors are also patrolled by angry doorman, who on more than one occasion prevented me entrance into my own hotel! It felt like tryng to get into a trendy nightclub at times.Worst experience by far was on our last night (hoping to get a good night's sleep in preperation for an 11 hour flight!). Having played host to a high-school prom, the hotel obviously allowed a load of the recent graduates to rent rooms. Cue a night of screaming, banging, singing, running around corridors, etc. I've stayed in numerous hotels around the world, and never experienced noise like it. Even my university halls were quieter. At 3am, I finally caved and rang the front-desk. The phone rang for 5 minutes before finally being picked up - We'll send someone right up sir - which of course they didn't. It got to 4am when I eventually went out into the corridor myself to try and reason with them. In fairness, they did start to quiten down, but it was a draining and restless night to say the least.Ironically, despite the dark gloom of the main hotel, the rooms are suprisingly and dissapointingly bright at night. A combination of the cheap curtains, and the fact a spotlight shines directly at the windows... used to highlight a 50-foot high fashion advetrtisment emblazoned on the side of the building. That, in itself sums up the general cheap and tacky feel of this hotel.A hotel with a great legacy destroyed by pretentious owners. Avoid like the plague.

<Author>hellolizzie3
<Content>multiple personality disorder service We booked a room at the Roosevelt for a girl's night out in Hollywood. I have to say that the service resembled a person with multiple personality disorder. The valet  check in were more than polite, they were both extremely nice. Our towel boy and server during the day at the pool were outstanding. However! At 11 am there were no chairs available around the pool (the hotel allows locals to come use the pool without checking keys, i know because i am local and i have friends who do this). So we were relgated to a sectional couch at the back, a nice spot but unfortunately shady. At 4 pm we were informed our section was going to be cordoned off for VIP and that we would have to move. This was after spending the afternoon and $300+ from the bar/restaurant. The staff was informed if they could find us seats around the pool sitting together we would move, but that aside we weren't leaving until 5. They left us alone for the most part after that.Going back up to our hotel room to ready ourselves for dinner, one of my friends brought a beautiful bottle of champagne for us to drink while doing so. Calling room service I was told they would not send us up flutes or even wine glasses, but we could call the pool and they might send us up some plastic flutes. (WHATever). The pool sent up plastic beer cups. Um, NO! I sent the poor man back downstairs for either plastic flutes or glass glasses. The thoughts of my friend in terms of service versus labor cost, they had to endure 3 phone calls and 2 trips on the part of the server to finally send us up glass wine glasses. If they had done it the first time, it would have been far less hassle in terms of time and money. Either way you slice it, it's ridiculous.I do have to say that the room and our view was gorgeous, they supplied is with Fresh brand amenities (my personal favorite), the sheets and towels were all top quality (even though some of the towels had a Ritz-Calrton label) and we had a wonderful time. This hotel needs to offer in the way of service what it can offer in the way of fun. And it would be nothing more simple than common consideration and even just attending to the most simplistic of requests.

<Author>SFGuy35
<Content>Hurry Up and Wait at the Roosevelt The Roosevelt is known for being a bit of a Hollywood scene (or at least it was a year ago) which does not interest me, so I wouldn't have stayed there had it not been for a good deal through a business associate. But I was intrigued to see the property.First of all, arrival is a nightmare. The valets were so behind on a Saturday afternoon that traffic was backed up all the way down the side street next to the hotel. After waiting for a minute I swung around and parked on Hollywood Boulevard. The line at reception was 20 people long, and took forever -- one gets the feeling the young women working the desk were not hired for their brilliant interpersonal skills.Over to the elevator, and there's a crowd there as well. One of the two elevators is broken, and people are waiting up to a half hour for a lift. Finally making it to the room, and yes, it's nice -- due to a problem with the reservation I've had to get a nicer room (long storyand not the hotel's fault), and it's quite the space -- two bathrooms, a sitting area, all very well designed, a step up from thecheese-modern Standard. But then I open up the laptop to get some work done and the complimentary WiFi is barely functional -- a website takes 5 or 10 minutes to load, if it loads at all. It was like that all weekend.I went to check out the fitness center, but even though it was mid-afternoon, it seemed closed, and very small. The party scene around the pool was amusing (if a little crowded for someone just interestedin a swim). Every girl was a Hollywood proto-starlet, every guy was a steroid-enhanced dude in a baseball cap. Getting my car back, even though it was parked right there in the parking lot, was a nightmare -- a line for the valet window, then a giant crowd of angry people outside, and it took about 45 minutes. I learned quickly to avoid Hollywood Boulevard which was always snarled with traffic, and just walking to the Hollywood and Highland mall to buy a swimsuit was a challenge. Again, the room itself was lovely, with a large bed and a great shower with nice soaps and stuff. Rowdiness on lower floors (and especially around the pool) seemed like it would have been a nightmare for anyone wanting to sleep, but I didn't have a noise problem, other than the deafeningly loud fan that I couldn't figure out how to shut off until I called the front desk the next day (hint: it was the giant switch in the circuit breaker). So, if I was paying full price, I'd never, ever stay here again. While the infrastructure and design is nice, the service level is nonexistent, and every aspect of the hotel is geared towards a scene not a happy traveler.

<Author>dahliablue
<Content>Great Girls Getaway I almost switched hotels after reading some of the reviews. I really wanted to stay somewhere that was part of the scene for a girls' weekend in L.A., but got nervous after reading the negative comments. Once we got there, however, I was glad I stuck with my original choice. The hotel had great ambiance. I loved the cavernous effect with the dark hallways and low lighting. It made it feel like old Hollywood, but with a modern twist. The crowd was a good mix of young privileged partyers and wealthy grown-ups and there were a few events going on that made us feel as though we were at the place to be. The staff was excellent; very friendly and accommodating. Our room was quirky with the bathroom through the closet, but the beds were cozy and it was plenty of room for three of us. The rooms didn't have the level of luxury that you might find at hotels going for this rate in other cities like The Omni in San Diego, but in L.A., this is what you get for the money; clean, comfortable, hip and right smack in the middle of everything. I can't wait to go back and spend some time by the pool, which was great for people watching, (and for good food and drinks).

<Author>SignorSummer
<Content>Very good, but not a World beater I just spent five nights in a Studio Suite on the tenth floor of the Roosevelt. It cost around $370 per night. I was there on business, so the first thing I wanted to do was go online, but the wi-fi in the room wasn't particularly dependable.So I settled into what was a fairly well-appointed room. Two bathrooms, a very comfartable bed, lounge space with a sofa separated from the bed by a wooden screen.The room was quiet, but luckily the poolside bar was buzzy, if pricey. I've partied at the Standard on the Sunset Strip before, but the Roosevelt apparently now rivals it as one of the spots to head for in Hollywood. Paris and Lindsay weren't about, but there was a decent atmosphere and a smattering of poseurs. Because of that, don't stay in one of the surrounding Cabana rooms if you want to get any sleep.Room service was prompt, friendly and efficient, as were the front desk staff. Taxis wait on the street so you don't have to and I can't comment on the restaurants as I didn't use them.

<Author>jetlagnow
<Content>Stayed here a while ago... was a little bit disapointed I haven't stayed here in a while, but I did a couple years ago and was sort of disappointed. The hotel itself has an incredible history (with the Academy Awards having been here for many years) and its fun to just drop by the hotel lobby and walk around or get a cocktail at the lobby bar and soak up the atmosphere. But when I stayed here one night, I was given a room out by the pool. The room was not very clean and the pool area was noisy (partiers walking out there late into the night). It is a beautiful hotel on the exterior, but I was underwhelmed by this bare bones hotel room. The sheets were itchy. Don't know why. Didn't sleep well. I expected a romantic, old fashioned Hollywood Inn that had that 30s-40s retro feel with very clean rooms. Instead it was more of the kind of party room you would get in Palm Springs near the pool area of a small to midsize hotel during Spring Break. I'm sure the hotel probably has other rooms that are more what I was thinking of. But I was slightly disappointed anyway. The hotel restaurant has ugly decor that looks like something someone's grandmother picked out. Not retro and not period style, like it should have. Food was over-priced and mediocre. They need to develop the lobby bar area into a more user-friendly part of the hotel. It's too small. They should spritz up the outside of the hotel with fresh paint and some cool old-style awnings. Class it up a bit. And retro-fy the rooms back to the old style.

Staying at the roosevelt you just have to understand that a lot of events are held there.The pool area and tropicana bar are beautiful. I am sure the cabana rooms and great to stay in too.

<Content>Loved it! Will stay again! My husband and I stayed for nights and loved it. We got the Cabana Room Balcony which overlooked the pool and Tropicana Bar. The Chinese Mann's Theater is right accross the street and there is a shopping mall with several restaurants. The pharmacy around the corner (to the left and across the street) has some groceries. <Content>Party here, but don't stay here! Just got back from an overnight trip to LA to see Wicked at the Pantages. I would not pay over $100 a night for this place.It IS in a great location though. Across the street from Mann's Chinese theater and the Kodak Theater and shopping centers. You can walk out the front door onto the Hollywood walk of fame and other Hollywood tourist attractions.

<Author>coolchickie76
<Content>Nice hotel! We stayed 2 nights Feb 20-22. Price awesome on Priceline!The hotel staff were all very nice and soooo helpful. The girls at the front desk were very pleasant which was a nice change from other hotels. Andrea, the concierge, was also great and she actually seemed to want to help and was always smiling. She recommended a restaurant Bella's which was down the road from the Roosevelt. It was Italian and me being Italian I was a little nervous b/c it was right on Hollywood Boulevard, I was thinking tourist trap. But it was really good and the prices were reasonable. So thanks Andrea on that call.The lobby and the halls were very dark like other reviewers have stated but it wasn't bad, it just seemed swanky to me. The elevators sucked though, they took forever (but no big deal, we were on vacation). One night all the keys didn't work in the whole hotel but the staff were very helpful and apologetic so it wasn't that big a deal. They had a glitch in their electronic system.Rooms were fine, no complaints other then sink leaking in bathroom. Beds comfy and rooms were big enough for us. Wi-Fi fine from where we were in our room (408). Not much to talk about, just a normal room, nothing over the top!No ghost stories here, even though I was freaked out before we went from reading other stories. I just was scared a little when I heard any noise. But my son (who we didn't tell that it was haunted) told me that in the middle of the night, on his way back from the bathroom he thought I was standing by the tv but then realized I wasn't standing there. That freaked me out just a bit so who knows!!!Bars at the hotel were okay but VERY expensive---2 drinks $27.00 (and they were not big at all, a couple sips you're done)!!!! We tried to get into Teddy's (where the celebs go) and the girl at the door was verrrrrryyyyyyyy mean and just looked at us like we weren't there. The guy said it was for Guests and reservations only! We asked about reservations and he said they need to be made 2 weeks in advance which I'm sure is a lie. The fact is if you are not a celeb or millionaire you aren't getting in! Tropicana Bar was dead, not too many people there but I hear it becomes one of the hot spots during the summer. It was pretty nice there with the pool and some fire pits (I suggest bringing your own drinks in if you could, because atmosphere was cool and no one where you walk in so you can save yourself a buck making the drink in your hotel room first then just hanging out there).

<Author>StephanieCincinnati
<Content>Great Location! Would definitely stay again! Great Location! Would definitely stay again!My husband and I were very pleased with this hotel. The best part about it was definitely the location. It right on the Hollywood Walk of Fame. As soon as you walk out the front door you see the stars on the sidewalk. It also steps away from the Chinese Theatre and the Kodak Theatre, where you can see a great view of the Hollywood sign. There a lot of good shopping and restaurants nearby too. If the main point of your trip is to see Hollywood, you probably wouldn even need a car (and could avoid the steep price for valet). Jimmy Kimmel Live is filmed right down the street and they give away free tickets when you walk by.The hotel itself is obviously very old, but has undergone several renovations. The rooms are decorated very modern with unique artwork. I guess because the hotel was built so long ago the layout was a little strange ?you had to walk through the closet to get to the bathroom. The bathroom was very small but was sufficient. There was little furniture in the actual room ?you either sat on the bed or on the one desk chair. There were two big windows which made the room look bright and cheery. One small annoyance was that our room faced Hollywood high school and the band was practicing on our first night, but it wasn too bothersome. The only thing I would say needed improvement in the room was the bed linens or actually lack of linens. It might sound petty to some but there was no top sheet on the bed and the comforter had a couple stains.Apparently there are several stories of ghosts at this hotel but luckily (or unluckily depending on your viewpoint) we didn run into any! The lobby is extremely dim with candles lit all around giving it a somewhat spooky feeling (especially if you read the ghost stories before you go!). I would definitely recommend this hotel to anyone visiting Hollywood who wants to be in the heart of it all! We booked our room on a name your own price website and got a great deal (I was shocked it was accepted!). I not sure the rooms are worth the actual prices Ie seen on other websites ($200-$250) so I would check around for the best price before booking!

<Author>shellmjb
<Content>Pleasantly suprised We stayed at the Roosevelt from the 1st Jan - 6th Jan and were tempted to change our booking based on the number of bad reviews we read. However we are certainly glad we didn't! Yes the hotel is dark but it is part of it's ambience, and its unique interior design set it apart from the numerous other hotels were it not for a name would be almost interchangable. From the begining we got a good feeling, the bell boy was friendly, chatty and very informative. Our room was clean and reasonably spacious, and when we did have a plumbing issue in the bathroom the staff were polite, helpful and prompt. We had breakfast at Dakota most mornings and again found the staff to be great and the food delicious. The location is superb and you are as central as possible most of the must see LA. While I could see it would probably not be an ideal choice for people with a younger family, my husband and I both loved our stay there and would most definately stay there again if in LA.

<Content>Embarassingly horrible experience. Went to the Hollywood Roosevelt for New Year's at the Dakota restaurant. They advertized a spectacular prix fixed dinner on New Year's Eve and we were told that the price was $100.00 per person. When we arrived, we were warned by the parking valet that 1000 people were expected to show for the huge party and that the night might not be as expected since we were a couple in our fifties. We explained that we had to access our dinner reservations and gave up the car. The spectacular dinner was a tiny appetizer that could easily fit on one forkful. The waitress said it was foie gras but I am very familar with foie gras and the appetizer I ate was only pate'. My date had soup which was the only decent appetizer on the menu. For the main course, the menu said that one choice was a 2 1/2 half pound lobster out of the shell. Again, the portion was only 2 or 3 forkfuls with no vegetable or potatoe or salad. My date's dinner was 2 tiny lamb chops undercooked with no sides. We were both very hungry when dinner was over and ate the desert which we normally pass on. We each ordered only one glass of wine during dinner and when the bill was presented, it was $550.00. We questioned the manager on such a gross discrepancy of what we expected and we were told that there must have been a miscommunication as dinner was $200.00 per person and an $85.00 gratuity was included in the total cost. I was so embarrassed for my date who was visibly upset but being the gentleman he is, paid the bill without contest. He did tell the manager that the dinner was certainly not worthy of 200.00 but she just shrugged her shoulders. We then went to the party at the pool. Amazingly, the door man let us in but for the dozens of young people in line behind us who paid $100.00 just to get into the party (that offerred a fee for service bar), the dorrman told all of them that the party was filled to capacity and he couldn't allow any more bodies in there. People began to loudly protest, but the doorman just shrugged and said, Sue me. The blatant disregard for custormer service, the grossly unacceptable dinner, and the exhorbitant fees connected with this evening should be a warning to anyone who is even considering dining, visiting, or staying at this hotel.

<Author>Sailsand
<Content>Roosevelt, home of the stars and expensive bars We checked into the Roosevelt on Friday for a little RR. I was excited to be back at the Roosevelt as we had stayed there before, and had a great time. I had requested one of the Cabana rooms, which are the ones by the pool that allow access to the Tropicana Bar, one of the LA hotspots. We were a little dissapointed to have missed the Victoria Secret Party the night before, but still kept our spirits up with a couple of cocktails from the bar ($26 plus tips for two bloddy marys). Our room was super deluxe with a great patio next to the pool, the corner spot was secluded enough that we didn't feel like we were in a fish bowl. Rooms service and maid service were prompt and attentive, and for a change they really won't disturb you if you leave the Do Not Disturb sign on your door, a variance from most hotels where maid staff take it to mean knock really softly. The action at the pool bar was less than we could have hoped (we heard that the summer months the place is packed) but it was nice for a couple of drinks before heading out. We ended up staying an extra day we were having so much fun...I would reccomend the Roosevelt to anyone visiting LA who wants to play movie star for the weekend, just be ready to pay movie star bills as well. The room was about 500 per night with taxes, and drinks were pricey as well.

<Author>glamourpuss1000
<Content>Excellent all round We stayed here for 4 nights as a friend recommended it, we found a great deal on a website and paid for the basic room.On arrival we were upgraded to a Cabana Room, I can only describe it as fabulous.You are given a typed sheet of instructions to tell you the dress code for the Tropicana Bar and the admittance policy and the dates during your stay when certain areas of the hotel are closed eg lobby closed for MTV party, that sort of thing. Also on returning at night we had to go past about 5 security people to get to our room but such security is commendable in this day and age.The staff are all very pleasant, the pool is beautiful, they serve complimentary coffee there in the mornings.The restaurant and burger bar look great but as we were in Hollywood we wanted to eat out and about and particularly in the Hamburger Hamlet , only a few doors away, which if you sit in the window is the best location for people watching.Toiletries in the hotel are by Fresh, and the mini bar has great stuff. Given the fact it was $28 for 2 glasses of wine in the Tropicana Bar we tended to use our minibar as a fridge rather than consume its contents. We were erroneously charged for something from the minibar and queried it at checkout but it was immediately removed, no problem at all.Plasma TVs, comfortable beds, the location cannot be beaten.I can't see how it could be improved upon.

<Author>soleil17
<Content>Loved it and would stay again in a heartbeat! We were very hesitant to stay here given the plethora of bad reviews, but we were more than pleased with our stay.We found a booking code on Travelzoo for 119 per night. While this got us the cheapest tower room, the check-in clerk upgraded us to a Cabana Pool Room! The desk and concierge were all very nice and helpful to us.The room was huge and clean with a very comfortable bed and great bathroom. The clerk made it clear upon check-in that as a hotel guest we were permitted to bring up to three guests to the Tropicana Bar. The policy was clearly stated by them and upheld by the Tropicana staff. We decided to go have a drink at the bar and we found all of the staff very nice and courteous. We really don't understand all of the bad reviews about the rude service.We also ate at the in-house Dakota restaurant and absolutely loved it! We each had a Kobe steak and it was one of the tastiest steaks we've ever had in our lives (and we've had Kobe steak in Kobe). The restaurant staff were also friendly.Yes, the lobby of the hotel is dark - but it's massive and Moorish architecture. It's true to its past. It is what it is and we felt it would have been a shame to turn the lights up and ruin the atmosphere and architecture.The hotel has two laptops with free internet connections in the check-in area which we thought was a great nice touch.The hotel is also only about a block from the Hollywood/Highland center and the metro stop there. For all of those who say don't take the metro we disagree! We thought it was great! We took the FlyAway bus from LAX to Union Station and the metro the rest of the way to the hotel. It only cost us $4.50! Two weeks later we stayed at the Hotel Mosaic in Beverly Hills which uniformly receives good reviews on TripAdvisor. We agree that it is a great hotel, but we liked the Hollywood Roosevelt more! All in all we loved it. Maybe the management has gotten the message, or maybe everyone who stays there hoping to see a celebrity and doesn't writes bad reviews. Whatever the reason, we disagree with the bad reviews.

I'm talking NY Bungalow 8 level of bouncer action - they did everything but frisk me. They prevented my partner bringing her friend in to pick up a present from our room. This would be understandable if Tom Cruise and Katie Holmes were poolside with Paris Hilton and Simon Cowell, but these 'events' seemed to be made up of a crowd of wannabes desperately hoping the next person to walk in was famous on any level whatsoever. The Cabana rooms are small, pokey and dark, with laughable 'patios' and the level of service (apart from the sparkling car valets) is surly at best. Did I mention the rolling hotel power test that meant I had to shower in the dark? A blackout they announced via a note delivered at 5am? And upon my complaint suggested I might like to shave by flashlight? We all know what to expect from hip hotels (poor service, dark rooms, happening bar action), but this place makes the Hudson in NY look like the Four Seasons. And because of its proximity to Hollywood's tourist ground zero it never really manages the full conversion to style hotel. I tried it because I had read good things in various style bibles in the UK, and all the good hotels in West Hollywood were full. Don't make this mistake!Unless you're a REALLY desperate Hollywood wannabe, or you've got a fetish for being near Mann's Chinese and the select audience that brings.

<Author>lagunadallas
<Content>I quite enjoyed it... Despite some shaky reviews here, I booked the Hollywood Roosevelt because I wanted something fun for a quick 1-night stay and didn't want to spend $400 on one of the 5-star hotels. It definitely served its purpose well. The location is excellent, though quite the mobbed tourist scene on a summer weekend (as expected). The lobby area might be dark, but it has been very attractively renovated and captures the older feel of the building with a contemporary twist. The service throughout was friendly enough, never rude or snobby, though not of Four Seasons caliber. My room was as expected --- small, rather dark, though clean and nicely renovated. The bathroom was absolutely tiny, which is often the case with hotels in older buildings, and water leaked from a gap between the glass partition at top of the tub and flooded the floor after a brief shower.I had plans all evening and wasn't around to spend time at the Tropicana bar, pool ,or restaurants, though they all looked like a lot of fun. The Roosevelt isn't the best hotel in L.A., but for the $179 I spent, I thought it represented a relatively good value compared to other options on the Westside. I'd definitely go back.

<Content>Only for the Brave! I stayed here for 3 nights in July. Which to me is not right, for as a guest of the hotel you should be able to use the pool when you want and not have it domiated with non-guests.This hotel is definately catered for a younger crowd, as I am 25 I did not mind it. The location is great for Hollywood.I would return to Roosevelt but as for LA, this is my 8th time there and I must say it seems to get dirtier every time. Being from Sydney which is very clean, it is a shock and something that I do not think you can get used to.

<Author>A TripAdvisor Member
<Content>Great Location - Needs a change in management I just returned from a 3 night stay at the Hollywood Roosevelt. I had read some of the previous reviews before booking - and some of what others said was accurate.The walls are very thin - bring earplugs. We could hear the couple in the next room, and it appeared they were having a normal conversation (i.e. no yelling or loud voices). One of the nights we stayed was a Saturday night, other guests were extremely loud when returning to their rooms at 3:00 a.m. ?it sounded like they were inside our room. I suspect this is the norm for older hotels ?sound-proofing was not the science it is today. The room dcor is nothing special ?dark paint, black  white mural over the bed - very minimalist, not what you would expect from a place with such great history. The bed was VERY comfortable, although I thought housekeeping made a mistake when I noticed there was no top sheet ?just a duvet. The air-conditioner was very noisy, we opted to shut it off and sleep with the windows open instead.The pool was a HUGE disappointment. I always stay in hotels with pools as I like to go for a swim after a long day of sightseeing ?I was shocked to return at 4:00 p.m. and find the pool packed with non-paying guests! It appears the pool and the Tropicana bar - which is adjacent to the pool, are the N?spots for the 20-something crowd of Hollywood. Many of the hotel staff let their friends in, and one morning I observed one of the pool guys placing reserved placards on 50% of the lounge chairs at 8:00 a.m. in the morning. I spoke to the front desk about this and was told that only hotel guests use the pool ?this was a bold face lie, as I had over heard one of the pool staff talking to a group of 8 pool users about driving home and coming back later for drinks - most of the sunbathers at the pool had car keys with their belongings ?not hotel cards.If you want to be seen and be in the centre of the action ?this is the hotel for you, if you want comfort and luxury - go elsewhere.

<Author>A TripAdvisor Member
<Content>Never again What have they done to this hotel with so much history? I have stayed at this hotel twice before and have always had a nice comfortable time. When I had a short business trip recently, it was logical to stay at a place that I knew I could trust. Big mistake, the moment I walked in, I could tell something drastically had changed. To start of everything was black, the walls, the floor and the staff dressed in black. Felt like I was in a Dracula film with all the gothic furniture. This darkness seems to be a growing trend with some hotels across the States. I could not find my card key in my bag the lobby was so poorly lit and people were almost walking into each other, I kid you not. My room was frightening. The room was black, the bathroom light was red and to top of it. A huge photo of a man with bright blonde hair in a black jumper was above my bed looking down at me. My friend had to cover it for me with a towel, so I couldn see it. They charge to for coffee and teas in youe room too, that the first time for me! The only advantages are the great locations near by; if youe tourist it all at your doorstep. None of the staff were rude to me, that a plus, but I will never stay here again. It a shame because I had a big group of us going next year, but it safe to say I will be taking our business somewhere else. It is a shame the hotel has been taken over, it has lost all its glamour and famous history.

<Author>A TripAdvisor Member
<Content>Not my cup of tea As other posters have stated, the hotel is very dark. Our room was a dark brown and with hardly any decorations in the room it seemed depressing. On one of the nights we stayed, the BET awards after-party was held at the hotel. While that was impressive, it made it impossible for us to leave without breaking through the tight security and standing out like a sore thumb. We tried to leave without walking through the middle of the black-tie event, but they had all the entrances and exits blocked. I even heard someone say, No, this is not going to happen, when she saw our family standing there trying to find a way out. Her reference was to the fact that other hotel guests like ourselves were not going to be tolerated walking around when all we wanted to do was leave our room and do some shopping.I would not stay here again.

<Author>A TripAdvisor Member
<Content>Would Not Stay at Roosevelt Again My husband and I frequently stay in hotels for weekend getaways and I must admit this is the first time I have stayed in a room where I just did not want to be in the room. Generally I enjoy breakfast in bed, but at the Roosevelt I could not wait to get out of the hotel in the morning.To be fair I think whether or not someone likes the Roosevelt depends on what you are looking for in a hotel. So I will list the positives and the negatives.Positives- 1. The front desk was very nice and we were upgraded to the Cabana section of the hotel so we had access to the Tropicana during our stay. I'm not sure what is so great about the Tropicana, but if you are looking for $14 drinks then I guess this is a perk.2. We had dinner in the restaurant, the food and service were excellent. I ate the veal 2 ways and it was incredible. Negaitves-1. The airconditioner did not work properly and our room stayed a consistent 79 even though we set the thermostat lower. We were told engineering was working on this, but during our 3 day stay nothing ever changed.2. The room is very, very, dark. The walls are painted chocolate brown and the lighting is very bad. The unscreened window opens to the street so we did not open the windows. There was not enough light in the room for me to comfortably read a book.3. You can easily hear you neighbors talking, listening to the radio, or watching TV.4. The bathroom more closely resembled a jail cell than a luxury bathroom. The room is concrete, the shower is concrete. There is no tub or any hint of luxury.5. The concierge was not very helpful and insisted that he must make us reservations at restaurants rather than given us some options and letting us make our own decisions.In summary, I would not stay at the Roosevelt again. When getting away with my husband I look for a luxury room and amenitities. It appears this hotel is for people who want to be seen at the pool and the Tropicana bar. The pool is nice, but it does not make up for the lack of quality in the rooms. I would so say the rooms are lower in quality than the rooms in any lower priced chain hotel.

<Author>Jake029
<Content>Excellent Stayed here for 3 nights in November. Requested a room on a higher floor and after being offered a larger room on the 4th floor, we were eventually found a room on the 11th floor. Would definately stay here again if we wanted to be close to Holywood Blvd.

<Author>A TripAdvisor Member
<Content>short on good and long on bad.... My husband and I went with another couple to the Roosevelt recently. Our suite was pretty nice - a large room with some design-junky furniture overlooking the hills. It had a white leather banquette and a spray-lamp and a lot of interesting art. It was quite a nice room. Got room service once and it was actually very nice and prompt.But the fun kind of ended there; first of all, the other couple booked and paid for a junior suite on expedia. The Roosevelt told them there were no more junior suites and because they went through expedia, they wouldn't be able to get the suite. They were relegated to a standard room - which was about 1/5th the size of our suite. Beware - don't let the front-desk people at the Roosevelt take advantage of you like that. I think there are several reviewers on this site that had similar experiences. If you pay $150 for what expedia advertises as a junior suite, you should get a junior suite. I've contacted expedia about this. The hotel should quit this consistent and suspect practice. Moving on, the ceiling vents in all the rooms on our floor were under a well-lit catwalk under the roof. So maintenance could (and did) get to look into the room, and you could hear whatever was going on in every other room on the floor. When people partied until 4:a.m. then had a fight, my husband and I were privy to every last dramatic detail. When another family ordered room service 3 hours later, we knew what they ordered. The alternative was to turn on the A/C which sounded like a jet engine. The vents in the other couple's room were worse. Bathroom was very small, out-dated. The main ventillation was into the bedroom (not good). The toiletries were great - but only *some* rooms got lotion and body-gel while others got shampoo and generic soap. The more I think about that, the angrier I get: Just give us all the good stuff! How much could you be saving? The Roosevelt's club is evidently the hottest club in the town. But as a guest, you can't go to the club. Don't try it, don't think about it, just leave it alone. It's not going to happen unless you book a $400 cabana. I talked to a guy who had a suite and tried to get in the club. A bouncer took him aside and told him he'd let him in if he paid him $350. Elevators: mind-boggling. Took some people 45 minutes to go down 12 floors. I got acquainted with the fire-well by the 2nd day.OK so the interiors of this place look nice and our room had a lot of style to it. There just wasn't enough good stuff to make up for the snobbery and alienation. I can't remember a time I paid so much to stay at a place denied me full access to its ammenities. Bottom line, this place cuts way too many corners because it thinks it can get away with it on unwitting tourists.If you want to get treated better, stay at the Le Montrose - same price but way more services and seamless luxury. Or the Renaissance, or the Bel Age. Or the Standard, or the W. They're all a similar price and they treat you like a..... guest!  
<Date>Apr 12, 2006

<Author>A TripAdvisor Member
<Content>Great hotel - beware pool drink prices It was a great hotel for young travellers (I stayed with two friends, all around 25 years old). Good location, fun people. Our room was cute, adequately sized and overlooked the Walk of Fame. We were a bit nervous driving to our hotel, as we passed some questionable neighborhoods and a friend had warned us that the Hollywood area was ghetto. But we were pleasantly surprised to find the strip of Hollywood occuped by the Roosevelt very nice. The pool is nice, nothing extremely special but cute. But drink prices were a bit insane. We paid $75 for a small pitcher of Vodka Lemonad that was way too sweet to even drink. We each had one sip and left the rest. Overall, a great experience. I would definitely go back, but avoid the drinks at the pool.

<Author>jano1932
<Content>OOPS! Being a movie buff we picked this particular hotel due to its history and P.R. write-ups. We thought the back entrance a bit odd, but persevered. Service personel were cordial and helpful. We were toured and shown the room where the Academy Awards had been presented. When we got to our room we were not surprised as we had looked at the rooms on the net. It had an upscale decor.As we settled down..to unpack I was shocked to realize that there wasn't a bureau. I called the desk and they were a bit flustered; bell boy sent up; flustered; a few phone calls..my last comment was did you expect me to hang up my lingerie in the closet?..when told I could use the closet. When it all settled we were slightly upgraded to a larger room with a bureau..and very accomodating. King bed, nice linens..but, as we settled in we began to notice the tired carpet, the chipped paint, the lack of continuity in the decor; the so-so view; the safe that had to be replaced with a new one; the bathroom that looked like it had been constructed from a used construction site...concrete floors that had streaks on them. There really was nothing that was excitable. The location was superior.We put on the happy face and began to explore.The first shock we got was that guests do not have access to Teddy's..the new club. It is advertised and sounds like you can use it..but, the truth is ..it is a private club , with a key..for movie stars to enter and do whatever they please. The pool bar is also excluded on some nights. It almost appears that it is a private playground for the stars. The service elevator was broken and the workmen used the single guest elevator so that getting up and down was dicey.The lobby, front entrance is unappealingly dark. You need a flashlight to see...It hides the gorgeous decor and ceiling. Now, thats the negatives..the dining room was splendid for breakfast. That was the only meal we had there. We would not stay there again.  
<Date>Jan 10, 2006
