<Author>A TripAdvisor Member
<Content>Close But No Cigar If the accomodations were half as lofty as the attitudes, this would be a fine hotel. The main areas, though dark, are suitably dramatic and set a cool tone. The rooms did not meet expectations. My middle aged husband and I were upgraded to a poolside cabana by a breathlessly excited reservationista who assured us we could bring two friends to the club that night. Unfortunately, it is not my idea of luxe to be interrogated by a twenty-something trendster armed with a velvet rope and a rubber stamp to get to my room. The room was clean and the linens were high caliber, but the bed itself was soft and lumpy. The rooms are high concept, mid-century inspired moderne but constructed strictly of cinder block, concrete and cold mirrored surfaces. On balance, it seemed like a stylish means of renovating an old motel without actually upgrading the infrastructure one iota. Wear and tear is starting to take a toll too. The concrete flooring in the bathroom was noticeably cracked and broken. Endless dark hallways with no elevator and no signage ensured that we roamed lost every time we wanted to leave. It was OK at $159 but would have been an outrage at the aleged standard prices of $500-$600/night.

<Content>Neat experience! My husband and I stayed here for 2 nights this summer while on a long vacation in California. I was quite suprised by the other comments!! I recommend just having them park it when you get there and leaving it and just walk places if you can!! I think this hotel might be better suited for younger crowds and couples. <Content>Fantastic time!!! My fiance and I drove to Hollywood from San Diego and decided to stay the night at the Roosevelt Hotel before our flight home the next day from LA back to Heathrow.We found a great offer on Travelzoo and paid $99 for the kingsize room.When we arrived at the hotel we was greeted by the valet car parking guys who took care of our car and took our cases out of the boot and into the reception area, the car parking charge for the night was $23. We then proceeded to the reception desk and was greeted by a lovely lady who was extremely polite and friendly, she told us that we had been upgraded which we couldnt believe and we had a poolside room all for $99. We was shown to our room by another member of staff who showed us where everything was and if we needed anything who to call etc, and also informed us about the poolside party which would be held later that evening and we could invite 2 friends along who were not staying at the hotel if we wished.The room was fabulous, the decor was second to none, the bed was so comfortable and the bathroom was sparkling clean along with the rest of the room, there was a cd player, and flat screen tv, bath robes, hairdryer, phone, mini bar.The prices of the mini bar were quite pricey so we didnt have anything from there and we ate out rather than in the restaurant as we wanted to see some of Hollywood. We had breakfast the next morning in the hotel restaurant which was fantastic the service was excellent and altho a bit pricey $60 with tip for breakfast it was well worth it.The only thing i would complain about is the lighting in the room it was a bit dark altho that it was in line with the decor but the lighting could have been a bit better.The pool was fantastic, and we would definately go back again and wish we had stayed there for a few more days - i would definately reccomend

<Author>A TripAdvisor Member
<Content>Wonderful service, beautiful hotel I was kind of freaked out by the complaints on this site, especially since I paid a lot more than I usually do for a hotel since I knew I'd be using the hotel to do a little work and would be spending more time in the hotel than I usually do on vacation. However, within moments of arriving at the Roosevelt, all my fears were wiped away. The staff was friendly and courteous, the room was lovely and clean. I had a fantastic sandwich from room service, I spent the morning lounging poolside with my free paper and later in the day journaled a bit in the quiet and gorgeous front lobby. I was there during the weekend and it was a bit loud, but I didn't expect it to be country-cottage quiet. It's in the heart of Hollywood and there's a club onsite and they had a party in the lobby. I didn't mind it at all, and slept fine, but anyone who would mind it shouldn't stay here, or should bring earplugs.I do agree with other comments that the springs did poke through the mattress and I did mention that to the hotel- and I thought the absence of a top sheet was kind of weird. However all in all- the helpful staff, the nice and relaxing rooms, the gorgeous pool, the historic architecture and the fabulous location made this one of my favorite hotel stays.

<Author>A TripAdvisor Member
<Content>Don't stay at the Hollywood Roosevelt There really is no excuse for such mediocrity, when the Renaissance around the corner offers every luxury for 10 bucks more.The king standard rooms I had were shabby and small, and I can honestly say that something went wrong every night of my stay. The aircon was broken twice, the bathroom flooded several times - both the impractical bath/shower and then the aging plumbing of the toilet. In fact, despite the hygeine issue, staff there did not offer me another room when the toilet was flooding the floor.Other irritations were the lack of mini-bar on floors 3 and 4, the phones which apparently do not always reach a connection downstairs (since everything was going wrong, it would have been nice to be able to report it by phone rather than having to trek down in person every day), and the awful elevators which often take minutes to arrive.I hear that the bar is pretty good, but unfortunately all I saw of it was the poor service and 1930's style rooms and amenities.I hear that the suites are actually renovated to a modern standard. That's great if you have that luxury, but the standard kings are awful - nowhere near the standard of a 2-star chain. My advice - pay the extra 10 bucks and go somewhere good instead.

<Content>could be a great hotel Just came back from long weekend stay at this hotel. First my complaints:1) Front desk needs better people skills. <Author>vacationfromchgo
<Content>Not a bad place to stay I travel to Los Angeles once a month and try to stay somewhere different each time. Based on recommendation from a co-worker that lives in L.A., I chose the Roosevelt for this trip.I made my reservation VERY last minute. Then read the reviews here and was very nervous about my stay. But decided to give it a try, and move if necessary.I arrived Sunday September 18 - that's right, Emmy night. A little trouble getting to the place - Hollywood Boulevard closed, parking lot closed until I motioned to the security guard and kindly told him I was checking in. Which he did without question. This was a true test: I arrive in my capris, t-shirt and flip flops, straight off the plane. The hotel is swarming with sequined gowns and tuxedos, humping with the post-emmy party in the lobby.Despite my clearly NON-celebrity status, everyone was VERY friendly - valet, check in staff, bellman.Reviews are true regarding the private parties in the lobby and pool. But I was able to enjoy both areas during my five day stay. And when you're in Hollywood - are you really hanging out at the hotel anyway? And isn't part of the attraction to a Hollywood hotel the chance star sighting? Those are the people in those parties.Room service was probably the best I've ever had: timely and absolutely delicious!I travel extensively and am VERY particular about the hotels I stay in. I have stayed in many european style hotels - which is what this is - and find them very comfortable. But, I realize that not everyone is into that, and if you're not, then you indeed won't like the Roosevelt. I believe the hotel is still renovating guest rooms; starting from the top and only down to the 8th floor as of my stay. I think that might explain the sparse furnishings and bare walls.I can't wait to go back!

<Author>devinevacation
<Content>Cheap renovation, Uncomfortable beds It is terrible what they have done to this historic hotel. The rooms have been VERY cheaply renovated, which basically means they took out almost all the furniture, painted one wall cocoa brown (with sloppy edging, bad painting) and put in beds so cheap you can feel the springs. The hallways to the rooms are also dark brown, making them dismal to walk through. And what used to be a beautiful, glamorous lobby now is now semi-gothic, dark as a cave, rented out for special events. And it's true that you can't access the pool as a paying guest after 7 pm. We were even hassled just wanting to SEE the pool around 6:00 pm. Even though it was teeming with people we were not deemed cool enough to be seen there. The sad fact is, once this hotel is done being the in place for the hipsters, it will become simply a cheap hotel stripped of its glamorous furnishings and past. Don't bother.

<Author>LambyHibs
<Content>Frustrating stay!!! We will never stay at this hotel again..........On arrival, first impressions were really good. The valet and the front desk staff were very friendly and efficient. However, from then on, our stay got worse and worse. On the 1st night there was a private event held in the hotel which went on until 2am and our room on the 4th floor vibrated until that time. We rang to enquire when the music would stop and we were told the hotel had no control over the event. We chose this hotel as an ideal location to end our 3-week stay in California and one of the attractions was the pool. However, the pool was unavailable to guests for 2 out of 4 days of our stay, due again to private events. The hotel bar was also unavailable during our stay. The general impression we got from the hotel is that unless you are attending an event and / or are a celebrity, you are not valued. This is confounded by the fact that we were told that 95% of guests are attending private events. It felt like we couldn't use the facilities that attracted us in the 1st place. To be fair, the front desk staff were understanding and as a result we were compensated with 2 free breakfasts and free parking. By the way, we recommend the chocolate chip french toast!!!If you stay at this hotel and are inconvenienced, we recommend you complain to the front desk and ask to be compensated. This is the 1st time we have ever had cause to complain at a hotel, so this illustrates the frustration we endured on what should have been a perfect end to our holiday.

<Author>jkeyser
<Content>OK I stayed here for 6 nights, in order to attend a convention in downtown LA, as I did about a year ago. On the positive side, the hotel had a nice location close to the Chinese theater and Hollywood/Highland (the one somewhat nice area of Hollywood Blvd.). Getting to the metro station was very easy. I didn't have any real problems while there. Unlike others, I actually found the staff to be quite friendly, but I never had any problems.I felt like this hotel was trying to be trendy and chic, but it just made some things wierd. As another person mentioned, there are no sheets on the bed - just a comforter. I assume (hope!) they change the comforter cover, but it still seemed wierd. The soaps and shampoos were all some sort of herbal something or other - fine but wierd.Furniture was fine, but a bit worn. I understand they've had a recent renovation, but I sure couldn't tell.I didn't eat at the hotel, but there was a good Gelati shop right nearby, and a good Thai restaurant a short walk the other direction.On the negative side, parking was expensive ($23/day - it went up $5 in the past year!). You have to pay separately for each computer you want internet access on. Hollywood Blvd. overall is not a particularly nice place (though the immediate region of this hotel is OK). Overall, I thought it was an OK place, but it's nothing luxurious.

<Author>A TripAdvisor Member
<Content>Terrible experience, such a waste of a good hotel! Even from the beginning of our stay at the Hollywood Roosevelt, we had terrible service. My husband and I checked in around 10 pm on a Friday night, and were told by the hotel that there were no rooms left, and that they had overbooked the rooms. Even though, we had made reservations 2 months in advance for a 3 night stay! We complained to the front desk staff and manager on duty, who didn't give us much sympathy. They were too busy attending to the other guests were were attending a party in the pool area. The management's solution to the problem was shipping us to another hotel, located 10 miles away! After coming in from a long flight, being tired, etc. we were VERY dissapointed that the Roosevelt could not accomodate us in any other way, despite having a confirmed reservation. They also could not guarantee us a room for the following night! They suggest that we call the next morning to see if there were available rooms. What is the point of a reservation, if you have no rooms available?!Apparently this happens more often than they like to admit, since many other guests checking in on the same evening faced the same problem. It seems the staff were more attentive to the party guests, rather than their own paying hotel guests! We did end up staying the 2 remaining nights at the hotel, only to find our room very small, dirty and dingy. There were huge dirt spots on the carpet! The pool area was off limits and limited to VIP access. We weren't even allowed to go into this area, which was guarded by security, even though we were guests of the hotel! The only good thing about the Roosevelt was the location of the hotel which is located right across the street from Gruman's Chinese Theater, Kodak Theatre, and the Hollywood and Highland Complex. After returning home from our trip, we contacted the management of the hotel. They did not even both to give us a call back! We will not be wasting our time and money on this hotel in the future. We'll be staying at a hotel where they value their guests!

<Author>flasugmag
<Content>Totally Hollywood, a strange stay..... This was a strange, but satisfying, stay from start to finish. The front desk people were very nice but explained that the pool would close at 3pm for a private event. It was about 1:30pm, I do understand that check in time was not until 3pm, so we were early. We quickly changed into swim suits, and rushed down, we really wanted to go in this historic pool! As we arrived, we were told the pool was closed. We asked really nicely if we could just briefly check it out. There were people setting up for the event who were obviously kind of mad at the sight of tourists with kids arriving and trying to swim. We did take a quick dip, but were pretty much glared out. Oh well, we did get a brief look. We were mildly dissapointed that our room did not face the famous Hollywood Blvd, but that feeling went away quickly as we watched some sort of red carpet being rolled out in the valet parking area below us. We joked that we might see stars ! We went about our day enjoying the area and all its wierdness. The hotel was a SUPER spot to be based to see all the action. The stores, the food, the famous sites, the new complex across the street, etc. This hotel is totally Hollywood. The elegance of the lobby, the ballrooms (you can peek in), the lounge, even the pool area, were fabulous. When we returned to the hotel, tired and a little overwhelmed, we discovered that there really WAS a red carpet affair going on in the pool area and there were in fact stars present. We actually got to take pictures from our room of people arriving. This was way cool, need I say more. My husband and I took turns going downstairs and standing with the real photographers. We never saw anyone except some dude I later learned was Magic Don Juan. (?) A lady in the restroom who was obviously leaving the party told me it was a party hosted by E! for Hugh Heffner and his lady friends. Wow. Overall, this night was pretty unforgetable.The next day, the lobby was closed because they were filming something! The hotel room was very modernly funished, low beds, a sitting couch, a nice desk, a big closet. I paid $189 for a room with two double beds. Yeah it was a little small, but this is an old hotel. It has been uniquely redone. A doorman told us they are striving to get away from the touristy crowd and recapture the hotel of the stars status. The lobby was unsurpassed in its elegance and overall ambiance, sort of dark and gloomy, but upscale like a castle. Cleanliness was great, bathroom was nice and even had great shampoo and conditioner! We were travelling with kids, and this hotel wasn't exactly very kid friendly, but that was OK with us. The service was OK, kind of snotty but this is Hollywood. I would stay again, hopefully without the kids!

<Content>If you like attitude and bad service the Roosevelt is for you The renovation of the hotel is all for show. The bell staff gave quite a bit of misinformation. Upon entering our room we had to double check that we were in a room and not a closet. I was shocked that for $300 a night we were staying in a box barely fitting for a single person. The online descriptions of their rooms as opposed to the one we got was COMPLETELY misleading. We required a roll away bed, and when it arrived it didn't fit in the room!!! We had to pull the mattress off the rollaway and lay it on the floor. It was the most uncomfortable sleep I've ever had in all of my hotel experiences, springs in my side is not what I would expect from a hotel held in such high regards. After our night on the town we returned planning on getting a little pool time in. Upon our arrival we asked what time the pool closed, we were told 2am. We were all ready for a swim and after making our way down we were told by a doorman that the pool was open only to those in Cabana rooms or on a guest list!!! We had paid $300 dollars for a box and couldn't even use the amenities of the hotel!!! The next day we made our way to the pool and though the food was great, the service left much to be desired. Our server didn't bring the correct amount of drinks we ordered, she brought us the wrong menu to order from, which we weren informed of until almost an hour later, now mind you, we had already been waiting with our tummies growling only to be told we still had to wait for our food to be prepared. We had to check out by 1pm and we inquired if we could still use the pool after our check out and we were told we could. So we left our things so as to not lose our spot, and went to check out. Upon returning to the pool we were greeting by an EXTREMELY rude guy working as a doorman for the pool. No one informed us we were only allowed 2 guests pool side for the room we had reserved. We tried to explain that we had been out there all morning, left our items to secure a spot, told we could return to the pool but he wouldn't budge. His attitude was horrendous!!! we understood that the hotel had it's policies, but he could've handled the situation in a totally different manner. He was fed up with us and told us if we had a problem to take it up with the front desk, so we did. We explained our issue to the front desk manager and he said that it would be no problem and he would speak with the rude employee. Upon returning to the pool he blew up and said we couldn't enter the pool area and he didn't care what anyone said, and stood by his reasons of doing his job. I found it odd that someone working the door had more say than a Manager. Disturbed and frustrated we gathered our things and left. The hotel staff left a bitter taste in our mouths after such a sweet weekend, not the best way to end our fun weekend. It wasn't so much the hotels policies that bothered us (although we found them ludicrous) it was the attitude, the lack of decent customer service. If this is what the new hot spots have to offer, I want no part of it. Not only was I a customer, I am a human being, I should never have to tolerate anyone belittling myself and my companions when I just want to receive services for which I had paid for.

<Content>Should Have Listened! In booking this hotel I read previous reviews but thought, everyone has their own opinion so I decided to go ahead and form my own.......Well, I should have listened! The check in was very unorganized as they were short staffed (by their own admission) and the room we were given did not look like the photos. Our bed was awful with springs poking us in the back all night long. Towles were a bit shabby as well. The next day I asked to be moved to a larger room, which they did, and this room was slightly better. Mattress was still hard and in need of replacement but towels were nicer. The bathroom has been renovated and the shower now has a half glass door, which caused water to leak all over when showering. The walls are paper thin and we had to call security one night as we could hear everything going on in the next room, including a fight. The hotel itself has been renovated but the new owners do not allow pictures to be taken.......what a shame that a Hollywood landmark with so much history does not allow its guests to take pictures to remember their stay. I found this very disappointing. The pool closes every night at 7 for private parties, once again alienating the paying guests. If the new management spent more time trying to make their guests happy and less time trying to be the next in place to be more people would write better reviews and therefore recommend this hotel. Party places come and go but good customer relations go along way. The best thing about this hotel is the location.

<Author>A TripAdvisor Member
<Content>Awesome Hotel! Great hotel! My girlfriends and I spent the weekend in Hollywood and made reservations at this hotel. While pulling up in our car, the valet staff was very courteous and helpful. The hotel lobby staff was just as courteous. While checking in, I had requested a room with a patio. Unfortunately, they couldn't accomodate our request, but said they can give us a 'cabana' room on the ground level (no change in price). They advised that it could get a bit loud at night due to the festivities that take place in the pool area in the evening. We agreed to this room and off we went in search for our reserved room. As soon as we opened the door, we were amazed at how awesome the room was! The only bad thing was there was only 1 king size bed for 4 of us girls. However, I was in awe with the room decor. The bathroom was so awesome and chic! We had a ground level patio with a lounge chair and table. Our cute bell boy brought our luggages from the valet area and updated us on the nights events. We were very excited to hear that since we have a 'cabana' room that we are entitled in and out privelages of the pool festivities. While everyone waits in line to get in where the party's at, we just had to flash our room key and confirm our room number and reservation name. The hotel restaurant was delicious and we were honored to have the wonderful service. We didn't have reservations, but they easily accomodated us after a 15 minute wait. The hostess and wait staff were very courteous and fun. After dinner we went to the pool festivities (didn't have to wait in the huge line) where we encountered Kimberly Stewart and Hank Azaria. The pool festivities were hopping and the drinks were great! Great place for anyone who wants to have fun and possibly hook up. At the end of the festivities, we went back to our awesome room. I would've had a good night sleep had it not been for the people walking and talking throughout the hallways during the early morning hours. After a few hours of tossing and turning (5:30 AM), we finally called the front desk to get the noise level toned down in the hallways. The walls must be really thin because 5 minutes after the call, I heard security asking the folks in the hallway to keep it down. The bed was the most comfortable I've slept in a looooong time! The only crappy thing is I am now ridding my ankles and lower shins of the bruises I obtained from the platform bed. My bad, I just kept accidently banging my legs on it everytime I passed by the bed (forgetting it was platform). All in all, this is a wonderful hotel and definitely a great place for the folks who like to party! I will definitely stay there again!  
<Date>Jul 31, 2005

<Content>Roosevelt: Hooker Haven My husband and I stayed at the Roosevelt over New Year's Weekend in '04. We were impressed with the decor and location, very convenient, but not impressed with check in service. Room service wasn't too bad. Room was great. However, we went to dinner New Year's Eve and when leaving found the hotel filled to brimming and more in the parking lot; a NY's Eve party was evidently being held in the hotel. The numbers of people indicated more bash than party. We returned after midnight and the hotel was overflowing with people. Many of them quite honestly looked like hookers or call girls, some were obviously transvestites, many with multiple men on their arms and overcrowding elevators to the upper floors with their partners. We could not get to our room. We tried in vain to find stair wells. After wandering through crowds of people and smoke, we finally were able to cram into an upward-bound elevator and managed to get to our room. The noise continued even on the 10th floor til well past 5:00 a.m. I was appalled to see that there was virtually no hotel security, anyone could wander in off the street and apparently did, and appalled that they allowed this sort of activity to go on so openly. What really got me though was seeing a family with young children in the same dilemma, trying to get up to their rooms. I can only imagine what the children must have thought.I wrote the hotel an email about our experience, hoping at least for an apology. We got no response at all; we never have. My family and I will never stay there again under any circumstances. If they continue to treat us and people like the Bermans in this way, when the celebrity train has passed them by, and it will, they will find themselves with no customer base.

<Author>notgoth
<Content>Should have left it alone The hotel has recently been overhauled with a $15m purse - and thankfully they stayed fairly true to the original dcor, mainly because they had to ?it a national landmark. However, the budget seems to have been entirely spent on the LOOK of the hotel, definitely not the FEEL. I can honestly say whilst I am not a big Hollywood night scene person, this is the worse place I have been to in LA for years. Not only did I have to pay $14 for a martini (more expensive than any of the leading NYC hotels and most of the LA hotels) but they didn even have any martini glasses. We had to wait over 20 mins for our drinks from the library bar (not books but hey it had plasma screens - TV is the new book right?), which had four other people in it. No, not four people deep queues - just four other people!! The bar steward would wander off mid-pour to help the cocktail waitress - of which there was one for the entire lobby floor. Upon leaving, we had to wait 20 mins for our car even though it was parked 10 feet from where we were stood, because the snotty valet supervisor was too busy helping people out of their range rovers and other bling cars. I watched in disgust as a family of four who were actually staying at the hotel, got out of the sedan and had to remove their own bags and carry them to the front desk - why? Because someone with a flashy car behind them needed their doors opened for them. This hotel has huge historic meaning - Shirley Temple practised her dance routines on the stairs in the lobby, the first Oscars where held here in 1929, Winston Churchill stayed here, Marilyn Monroe had her first modelling gig here, Errol Flynn hang out here- and whilst there is the argument that by doing up the hotel they have preserved it, finally driving away that night I couldn't help but think that they'd destroyed something instead.

<Author>A TripAdvisor Member
<Content>loved the Roosevelt My stay at the Roosevelt hotel was pretty good. I thought the rooms were sound proof (mine overlooked the carpark) and the staff were very friendly and professional. This hotel is a huge old but renovated place with heaps of style from Charlie Chaplain days. It took me a while to undertand the lay out of the hotel but once that was out of the way it was great. The pool area was so kitch with an art deco feel. really cool. I had the junior suite which was plenty of space for one person. The daily morning delivery of papers was great and the bathroom was groovy. The only problem was the toilet blocked but as I later found alot of toilets block in the USA. I would definatley stay there again. I loved it. It wasnt the best best best hotel in the world but for the price ($100) per night and the fab location it was well worth it. Just make sure your shuttle drops you off around the back of the hotel not on Hollywood Blvd. The back is actually where the front entrance is. Your first impressions will benifit if you do that.

Bellman were courteous and prompt with our luggage. The rooms were awesomely decorated although a little on the small size much like most of the hotel rooms in NYC The rooms were very, very clean. The open shower effect (only one clear frameless door on the tub) created water puddles in the bathroom after each use but we discovered it was just a matter getting used to it which resulted in the least amount of flooding. The rooms were extremley quiet and soundproof. The staff seemed very professional and friendly. Overall for the price, it was well worth the stay. The hotel is centrally located to most tourist attractions in the LA area and definitely a place we would stay at again.

<Author>A TripAdvisor Member
<Content>One of only two hotels you should consider in Hollywood... Stayed here January 2005 my third visit to this hotel. Have always had a good experience. Let's start with it's biggest selling-point - the location. Directly opposite Mann's Chinese Theatre, you could NOT be better positioned in central Hollywood. You have the Metro station within 2 minutes' walk, various small stores/restaurants at the Highland/Vine Centre a block further on, the awesome Hollywood sign overlooking the whole neighbourhood and the Hollywood Walk of Fame running right past the front door of the hotel. Hollywood itself, if you have not been there before, can come across as rather seedy, with many tacky tourist shops and, shall we say alternative residents. However it has seriously cleaned up its act over the past few years and now feels safe to explore, even at night. And if it is evening entertainment you are after, take a cab or drive a couple of miles into West Hollywood where you will find Los Angeles' famed nightlife along Sunset Blvd (House of Blues, Viper Room et al) Or try Santa Monica Blvd, a few blocks to the south of Sunset, for a wide range of gay bars/restaurants.Back to the Roosevelt.To the rear of the hotel is one of the most peaceful pool areas I have come across - shaded, quiet, relaxed, the perfect getaway from the noise and commotion of Hollywood Blvd out front. I have read reviews about the horrendous price of the valet parking - for this area, the fee is pretty standard and my vehicle was already brought around very quickly. Again, I have seen reviews that the rooms are not up to scratch. I have to say, the refurbished tower rooms (which were all completed in 2004 I believe) are fantastic. They are not in typical US style - much more Northern European, with a trendy, IKEA-feel to them, I can really see them appealing to Brits and Europeans much more than to Americans. The beds are low-profile with sleak, minimalist headboards and feather duvets/ pillows. The bathrooms, although small, are very modern and the housekeeping was excellent throughout my stay. Make sure you ask for a high floor room as the views are fantastic - either the Hollywood hills to the rear or the City of Los Angeles to the front. If you want a central Hollywood property with a very good standard of room, you really need to be looking at this one. Other than the Renaissance (which I have reviewed elsewhere) this is your best choice.  
<Date>Mar 19, 2005

<Author>SunnyC
<Content>Great Location We stayed with a group of five people in two rooms at the Roosevelt in December of 2004. The complex was obviously being renovated at the time to take the hotel back to its glory days when it was made famous for hosting the Academy Awards. Our rooms were both quite nice, however they were tight on space and the facilities were average considering the star rating of the hotel. There was a restaurant being built while we were there, but this meant that we were treated to below standard services in the majority of the hotel. I would check to see whether the renovations were finished if I were to stay there again. The good thing about the hotel was its location. Right outside Mann's Chinese Theatre and the Kodak Theatre there are heaps of tourist attractions right at your doorstep. In addition to this the bus stop is directly opposite the hotel and it is easy to get to most places in LA from that spot. I would also recommend not booking any tours before you leave Australia if you are travelling to Hollywood. Across the road from the Roosevelt there are heaps of different tour companies that offer great tours for discounted prices. There is also a good tourist information booth in the Kodak Theatre Complex and the people there can help you with loads of information and phone numbers for companies. The location makes up for a lot of the short coming in this hotel.

<Author>A TripAdvisor Member
<Content>Happy with our stay We stayed at the Roosevelt for 4 nights in late January 2005.We were a bit worried by the user reviews but they had a really good rate of $150 AU per night and we wanted to stay in Hollywood, because of the location and proximity to the Metro train. We were not disappointed. The room and bathroom were very clean and comfortable. We had a nice view over the city through big windows. The room was on the small side and the beds only double and a bit firm but we didn't find this a problem, and we are a family of 4! Found the staff at reception very helpful when questioned about local transport and activities. Housekeeping was prompt and polite when we called for more towels. Bell staff were happy to look after our luggage on the last day and arrange cabs promptly. The old foyer was lovely. We were warned several times on booking that the pool was still being renovated so that was entirely expected. The evenings were a bit cold to swim anyway. Had a look at the pool area and it should be very nice when completed. Found the Metro easy to use and the station is across the road ( but remember the machines with only accept NEW $1 bills for tickets!-as the tourist office told us after we had battled with it for 1/2 an hour). It is a very quick and cheap way to get to Universal Studios and Downtown LA. Also connects to Long Beach but trip is about 1 1/2 hours. The Hollywood area itself was interesting and we enjoyed the new shopping and restaurant complex. I would be happy to stay in this hotel again as a good value , mid range hotel.  
<Date>Mar 16, 2005

<Author>A TripAdvisor Member
<Content>can't wait to return! I surprised my boyfriend with a one-night stay at the Roosevelt on Sat. Nov. 20, 2004. We had driven out with some friends earlier that year and were interested in all the paranormal things we had heard and read about. We were also breathtaken with everything it had to offer, thus making us want to return to stay. So I looked online to see what their rates were, but I called to make the reservation. I booked a junior suite for one night at the price of $189, plus an $18 valet fee, but with unlimited in-and-out privileges. The valet shouldn't really be that much because the valet staff was average. The check-in staff was very polite. We were given a beautiful, large room, with a view of Hollywood Blvd. that we didn't even ask for! We were so excited! The room had a very modern CD player, a big swiveling TV, a couch, coffee table and chair, a dresser w/ a minibar.. a big beautiful COMFY bed with plush soft linen. The bathroom was awesome. It had an old-time Hollywood feel to it, and it included an amazing shower and a separate bathtub. Now i read a lot of the reviews and everyone's complaining about how the pool wasn't available because of renovations. If you're really going to be that intent on using the pool and/or jacuzzi (like me and my b/f were), find out! All i had to do was go online and click on the pool and it said it was going to be closed. I didn't freak out because I WENT PREPARED. However, the staff did inform me that they had a deal going with the hotel across the street (i think it's called renaissance, not sure) that the roosevelt guests could use their pool. Well, before attempting to walk over in our bathing suits, we took a stroll to inspect it. It was an extremely long walk through very public places where we did not want to walk in our bathing suits, wet or dry. And when we got to that hotel, we asked the front desk if they had a jacuzzi and the woman looked at us as if we were extreme idiots and huffily replied no. She made a horrible impression on us. thank god we weren't staying there. So, yes, we were disappointed about not having the pool, BUT we were prepared. Never assume anything, because obviously it leads to disgruntled people and disappointment. But it can be easily remedied by just asking the question is the pool open? One more thing that I should mention. I also read in a lot of reviews about how the staff cares more about any functions that may be going on in the hotel rather than their own guests. I disagree with that but I had a similar issue. My boyfriend and went to take the stairs up to the main entrance that leads you to Hollywood Blvd. There were no signs or anything saying that something was going on. There did happen to be a wedding and they were in one section of the room that wasn't in the way of the exit. But someone working the party(?) ran over and immediately stopped us and said sorry you can't go through here! He got right up in our personal space and was very rude about it. We were innocent..we didn't know. So, if they're going to have any sort of event...especially where this wedding was, make a sign. Other than that, we absolutely can't wait to return to the hotel...when we have money..because yes, it is expensive, but it's a wonderful experience. I also have a review about the Excalibur hotel in las vegas for any interested parties.  
<Date>Feb 23, 2005

<Author>A TripAdvisor Member
<Content>Not as bad as the worst reviews... I stayed at the Hollywood Roosevelt for business. There are some problems, but I think many of these are attributable to the fact that the hotel is old, and in an area that is only now receiving some attention for revival. It takes a little imagination to see the Golden Era of the though the hotel has been recently refurbished. For whatever reason, they don't use the front entrance as the main entrance anymore, which is a shame because your first impression is of a cramped den-like area, rather than the rather grand lobby where you can picture the way the hotel was back in the day. Details--like not being forewarned that the pool was closed for renovation, the overpowering smell of the deodorizers in the hallway and room, a worn school folder for the stapled menu and ratty photocopies of other information, and the lack of a top sheet on my bed--leave a sour taste for a $199 room. It could be that the nicer more expensive rooms are, well, nicer. The management company really should get its act together fast because it is almost there. I found all the staff really eager and helpful except, interestingly a front desk manager-type who was obviously sick of the service industry, waiting for that big break. On the flip side, the rooms are very recently redecorated, (this is not your grandmother's hotel) have CD players, down comforters, room service was outstanding (the food and the service) and the vibe is retro/funky/cool. The include a hip jazz/house music CD in the room to give you some of the background music that you hear in the lobby as you check in. The restaurant and bar look nice, although I did the room service option. The lobby is really grand. I hate L.A., so most of my negative feelings stemmed from feeling like I needed a bath the minute I got into the hotel just from riding there from the airport. The neighborhood is not nice but it IS Hollywood...the Walk of Fame, the Chinese Theatre, the tacky souvenir shops, and newer nicer stores at Hollywood and Highland's new mall. If your expectations are sufficiently lowered from luxury to nice and you aren't too sensitive or detail-driven, the Roosevelt is alright.  
<Date>Jan 31, 2005

<Content>Whatever your standards lower them Stayed here Nov 6th to 11th 2004 and overall I would have to say what a let down it was. The hotel seems to mainly cater for various functions that seem to happen every night and paying foreign tourists are just an unwelcome inconvenience. Obviously these are only my opinions and we still had a great time in LA, but do yourself a favour and book somewhere else.

<Author>A TripAdvisor Member
<Content>Wonderful- I would definately return! Myself and three friends stayed at the Hollywood Roosevelt for 3 nights in late September. Due to the previous reviews I wasn't quite sure what to expect but I was pleasantly surprised! On arrival, we went to the lobby (which was around the back of the hotel) which was small, but tastefully decorated. It was kind of annoying having to drag the luggage down stairs to go to the desk however! I was told by the guy on Reception that they were going to give it all an overhaul, as the steps caused a lot of problems. Anyway, my friends and I had booked just a standard room (the cheapest available) and were upgraded by the super-nice front desk staff to a Suite on the top floor! As far as Suite's go, I have had bigger at other hotels but it was still lovely to be upgraded! The room had a living area with a big comfy sofa and armchair, divided bedroom with two Queen Size beds, and two bathrooms. Having two bathrooms between four girls was definately a bonus! One interesting thing I noticed though, is the bathtub in one of the bathrooms appeared to be original despite new tiling and decor. The bathtub was made out of proper tough porcelain, not plastic, and the shape and strength of it, made me think it had a lot of age to it. This said, there was cracks in the porcelain around the plug hole. No big deal. The bathtub still did the job, and I figure it would cost a fortune to get fixed- and it's still better than modern junky plastic ones! The location of the hotel is superb if you want a Hollywood experience. Right in the middle of Hollywood Blvd, across the road from Manns Chinese Theatre and a shopping mall! Seemingly, Hollywood has started cleaning up it's act in the past few years. It isn't as glamorous as it once was, but is making vast improvements. Like I said earlier, the front desk staff were superb, we had some problems with a cab company overcharging us, and the hotel employees helped us out! They were always so friendly, and always remembered us! We dined at Theodores, the restaurant, for Breakfast one morning- and admittedly the waiter was rather pathetic. He tried to overcharge us (the account was added up incorrectly) and I asked to speak to the Restaurant Manager, who apologised and gladly rectified the situation. All in all, the rooms were clean, tastefully (if minimally) decorated, and the service and location was superb. I would definately stay here again! Additionally, when we were staying at the hotel, STING was staying there as well! We never saw him, but knowing we were under the same roof was definately an added bonus!  
<Date>Oct 31, 2004

<Author>Marcus_and_Wendy
<Content>A nice place to stay I stayed at the Roosevelt for two days in September 2004 and found it to be a pleasant hotel in a good location. Check-in was efficient and I was offered a choice of rooms. Being from way out of town (8,000 miles out of town), the lady was very helpful and suggested a room on the eighth floor (quieter up there) with a view across Hollywood Boulevard. The room was bright, spacious, modern and comfortable, with plenty of storage space, walk-through dressing room, safe, and nice touches like a coffee percolator. It felt clean and was serviced unobtrusively. My travel agent who booked the room in June told me in July about the renovations and closure of the pool, and they were not a problem. If I'd wanted to use a pool they offered an alternative hotel nearby. I had dinner one evening in the restaurant and, apart from the standard American propensity for rushed meals, it was a pleasant experience - interesting food, friendly and helpful service, a good wine list, and the historic ambience. The only negative experience was on the final day. I'd had my bags collected and stored in the morning, spent a great day at Universal City, then returned to the hotel to pick up my bags and get a taxi to LAX. I think the desk man must have had a deal going with a company on another planet because once he'd phoned for the taxi he made no effort to get my bags, told me there was no hurry, and got on with his work. Meanwhile I watched plenty of empty taxis cruise past the hotel while I waited 40 minutes for mine to arrive. When we got to LAX the driver seemed lost and had no idea where to find the correct terminal. an unfortunate end to an otherwise pleasant stay at the hotel.  
<Date>Oct 3, 2004

<Author>iluvla
<Content>oh how it has changed! we have stayed at the Roosevelt many times over the years and last year will probably be the last time unless there is a change in ownership.We have seen this once beautiful old hotel,loose all it's character as it was gutted in the name of modernisation.Gone are the comfortable furniture to be replaced by hard,plain and ugly chinese style stuff.We lost count how many times we banged our shins on the awful bed,whose mattress was too small for the frame,and oh so low.The wonderful art deco was replaced by bamboo sticks,but worst of all the lobby was cleared of seating for the guests and hired out to private functions,while guests were driven into what once was the basement and is now the reception area,small and like sitting in a pit,we sat and watched the complaints from other guests fall on deaf ears.It was impossible to sit in the evening and have a drink at the small bar as there were only a few chairs or high bar stools.Front doors were locked every time a private party took over the old lobby so we had to walk around to the back door and dodge cars as we crossed the carpark.The mezzanine,which had once had a display of pictures showing the history of hollywood,was reduced to a drafty open gutted space,said to be a bar one day..All the friendly staff who had been there for years left,to be replaced by others who seemed more and more stretched to service the private functions rather than the guests actually staying in the hotel.This is a hotel that has completely lost it's way..is it a hotel or a collection of function rooms? What really has angered us is the fact the hotel's website is SO misleading,not a word about the still ongoing building work...it's been at least 3 years now since it started and still isnt completed.We doubt it ever will be.It is sad as we really loved the old Roosevelt.

<Author>A TripAdvisor Member
<Content>great location but no pool I took this trip to cheer up my mother you just lost her husband. She has always been intrigued by Hollywood. The location of this hotel was great for star watching, as is close to Mann's Chinese theater, the Kodak theatre were they have the Oscars and the El Capitan were Disney holds it's premiers. Our room was clean comfortable with a spacious bathroom and a view of the Hollywood sign as well as Mann's. The front desk staff was courteous and helpful. When our room key was accidentally deactivated, security responded promptly. The room service staff was great. My only complaint is that the pool and Tropicana bar that they mentioned frequently on their website is closed from June through Aug of 2004 and nobody mentioned that on the website or at the time of booking. If you want to swim or sunbathe pick another hotel this summer. Other then the closed pool disappointment , I would stay at this hotel again. The metro station is located within one block of the hotel and is cheap and easy to use . <Author>cjennt
<Content>Hollywood in the Old Tradition Sure, you could stay at the more exalted Beverly Hills Hotel, but if you want the quintessential Hollywood experience, this is the place! I have stayed both in the pool cabaa villa and in the main tower. I much prefer and would recommend the cabaa; as the room is much more spacious and comfortable, not to mention quiet, except for pool noise which might be a problem in summer. The hotel is a historic wonder and is strategically placed in the heart of Hollywood Blvd. with Graumann's Chinese theater and other attractions, Walk of Fame within easy walking distance. The lobby area has the old Hollywood flavor coupled with 1920's style architecture and Spanish influences throughout; the hotel dates from 1927, the year of the first talking picture. The mezzanine level is a tribute to Hollywood history and is worth a look in itself. The famed Cinegrill in the Blossom Room was the site of the first Academy awards back in the late 1920's or early '30s. This hotel was literally a clubhouse for the likes of Errol Flynn who purportedly invented his recipe for gin in the backroom of the ex-barbershop. Nearly every star has trysted here, including Marilyn Monroe and the hotel has attracted famous politicians and literary figures like Ernest Hemingway. All in all, a fascinating place to stay and good service as well. Remember, get a room in the cabaa area; it's the best.

<Author>A TripAdvisor Member
<Content>what a waste of what could be a great hotel Stayed there Feb 14, 2004 (born and raised in LA and have tradition of staying in a different local hotel every Valentine's Day). Stayed on 6th floor in a junior suite--had to turn off the air conditioning becuase fan was so loud (not broken, just old and loud) you could not talk over it. The only good thing about the Roosevelt is the physical building itself--real 1920's era art deco blended in clsaaic Spanish California touches. The bar is awesome--but we and all other guests could not enjoy it since the hotel rents it out to private parties;we wandered too close by mistake as we were trying to find a door to the street and 5 security guards were upon us. To use mini-bar, you have to walk down to front desk to get a key (and give your credit card). Front desk gave us a key, but it did not work. Did not bother going down again for fear of having security think I was again trying to crash the private rap music party. Tried calling room service from our room for dinner--but after 50 or 60 rings and multiple calls they did not answer. Called front desk which acted like it happens all the time and they transfereed me to room service (without any apology or even mention of fact room service does not answer phone). When room service came, all the girl wanted to talk about was the private party--the one no one else could get into. Called room service again next moring for breakfast (actually had front desk connect me because they would again not answer call from our room) Tried ordering coffee, but I was told to just make it myself on the mini-maker in our room. Tried, but it was broken. I would not say staff (mostly all in their early 20's) is terrible, but the service is. My feeling is that it's management's fault--they simply give staff no guidance on how guests should be treated at fine hotels, with the result that the Roosevelt is a fine physical building but sucks as a hotel.

<Author>Meursault
<Content>Worse Than a Horror Movie- A Dump! Upon hearing of the old days of grandeur of this hotel, I was reluctant to stay here with some old friends but I thought that perhaps they had invested heavily in the refurbishing of the hotel and made it a top notch place to stay, was I ever wrong. Upon arriving around 1 am after a lengthly flight, half starving and dazed, I checked into the basement, where the staff was very rude, they did not even ask me how I was nor if I needed anything, they simply gave me a key and brushed me off. I walked up what seemed a hallway from an insane asylum, as I had been giving a room by the pool by the 'kind staff'. At first glance, I thought, this doesn't look good, considering that there were pools of water from the central ventilating shaft, leaking all over the place, streams of garbage, towels and dirty piles of what seemed like rotted food. I opened the door to the dirty and dingy room, thinking I was in some welfare hotel, upon entering I was disgusted at how bad it truly was. A dirty odor, smelling of foul stench, probably from the old rug which had blood stains upon it, entered my nostrils. This was really horrible and I was the first one to get there, considering my tired friends were still on the plane expecting a comfortable and safe room. I made a quick inspection of the room, from the broken sliding glass door which had no lock upon it to the terrible molded curtain that nearly fell upon my head. The beds had stains upon them, and they weren't even changed as if they had given me an previously used room. I opened the closet up and was startled to notice a 1950's style air conditioner leaking all sorts of water and fluid upon the wood and carpet, that was where the smell was coming from. The bathroom was even worse, to my surprise and horror, there was black mush in the old toilet, the rusted pipes were craclking and the mirror was very scary for it was blemished and aged. There were no towels, no soap, not even any toilet paper! The whole room had not been remodeled since the 1950's, for it was in the Cabana style, not even changed, I could not believe I was paying $150 a night for a room that looked like a prison chamber and a dump! When I tried to call the staff, they ignored my requests to get a better room. Attempting to use the bathroom, I found out that there was no water at all and the toilet would not flush! This was a complete disaster for me and when I attempted to get to sleep, I was awakened by some noisy generator that sounded as if it was about to explode. That night we looked for a place to eat and the area is dangerous, drug users, prostitutes all hang out there so I wouldn't advise walking around there and there aren't even many places to eat except dirty taco joints and a very expensive Mel's dinner. I would not ever stay here again, considering I was gimped out of a forture by the place. Be warned, do not stay here at all.

<Content>fantastic hotel We visited the Hollywood roosevelt in November 2003 for five nights.On arrival we were upgraded to a fantastic suite on the 11th floor.It was very spacious with two kingsize beds,and a huge bathroom which contained a wet room and a bath.The toiletries were plentiful and of excelent quality. we had a view of Hollywood blvd,and could see right into the forecourt of manns chinese theatre.We were also very pleased to find that we had a perfect view of the hollywood sign.The hotel was in a brilliant location,taxi to warner bros studios was $10,the tube to universal studios is a minute walk away and whilst on the tube is only a five minute ride.Mels diner is a great place to start the day, breakfast is well recomended and not too expensive.Next door to mels diner is the Max factor museum which contains loads of hollywood costumes and make up worn by the stars for example-marilyn,joan crawford. we were travelling with our 10 year old son who found the outdoor heated pool fantastic,and went for a few moonlit dips.I would reccomend this hotel to anyone.the sheer history of the hotel is overwhelming so dont let other reviews put you off.i would love to go back someday.

<Author>Samsie
<Content>Not as nice as it once was We last stayed here two years ago and since that time it has been in the throws of refurbishment. We had four nights there over the New Year and into Jan 2nd 2004.It felt deserted the night we arrived albeit at a very late hour. However, even during the day it was very quiet. The most number of people we saw in a given night was on New Year's eve when the beautiful people arrived in their droves for a New Years bash in the ballroom.The reception area in this hotel is now in the basement and not the lobby where it used to be. The lobby now looks completely except for a couple of sofas and a table in the middle of the room. The restaurant on this level is still there though again not many people were using it. The coffee shop place at the front of the hotel is closed.It took them many minutes to sort out a room for us as their computers were slow (overnight processing). Once we got keys we were shown to a room on the 4th floor even though we asked for a high floor. We had to ask them again to bring up our bags as they had forgotton to do so. Our room keys stopped working on the 2nd day and when the keys were reprogrammed they still did not work necessitating a further trip back to the front desk. They had it transpired misprogrammed the keys to open another room. They were apologetic about this.Beds were uncomfortable in the first room we had and it did feel very cold to begin with. It was also very minimalist in tone with also minimal counter space in the bathroom to place toiletries. We had a room change during our stay on New Years Eve as you could clearly hear all the noise during the soundcheck to the party (our room was above the Ballroom). The room change was swiftly dealt by reception with and our bags were efficiently moved to a junior suite on the 8th floor. Staff did try overall to make our stay pleasant and the porters were helpful when we checked out. There is a nice restaurant a block away called Hamburger Hamlet which is well worth calling into. We did not use room service. Its main saving grace is its proximity to Hollywood and attractions like Universal studios (the metro at Hollywood and Highland costs little and is easy to use) but if and when we return to LA we will stay in a different area.  
<Date>Jan 4, 2004

<Author>A TripAdvisor Member
<Content>Forget it! My wife and I stayed at the Roosevelt Hotel on 13/14 September at the start of our two week 'trip of a lifetime', impressed by their website and Cabana room advertising. Our first impression on check-in did not bode well - lots of furtive looks, comments and glances between receptionists. All became clear when we saw our reserved cabana room, which was not at all close to the pool and overlooked a noisy side room. A dirty and cracked handbasin, rusted bathroom fittings and a filthy carpet completed the room's attractions. Our immediate request for a room change was ignored. Staff quite unfriendly except for the porter.Main entrance to the hotel is locked during private functions leaving guests to wander aimlessly to find a way out. It is hard to see where the much lauded refurbishment has taken place - but certainly not in the cabana rooms. This encounter nearly spoiled our holiday - thank God for the numerous Best Westerns we stayed at thereafter, the rooms of even the worst one of which was infinitely better than our Roosevelt room. Its only saving grace is its proximity to Hollywood Bvld.

<Author>A TripAdvisor Member
<Content>"Poolside Cabana" is no big whoop My family and I stayed at the Roosevelt in July 2003 for our big family vacation at Universal Studios. Wanting something cool and art deco, we chose the Roosevelt based on its pictures on Expedia.....here's the thing - a) only if you stay in the TOWER Room (not the poolside cabanas - which are more $$??) do you even have a chance at the cool art deco room featured in the photo; and b) our poolside room looked (and SMELLED) like something from Motel 6 (or the Bates Motel). Old carpet, old bedspreads, a cranky a/c that leaked all over my clothes in the very small closet, a safe that didn't work 90% of the time, etc., etc... However, the staff was great, the tower room was beautiful, just what I imagined - very art deco/contemporary/zen. Would not stay there again.

<Author>Dutchbairn
<Content>You people are so wrong if you think the Roosevelt's sucks! My goodness. It really surprises me that people feel that a 3 star hotel should be double its rating and also remain the price they paid. The Roosevelt is a wonderful place. Clean, yes clean, and extremely helpful staff. Anytime that I had to speak to the reception, they were very courteous. This was our first experience of valet parking - also very friendly people. The gift shop, although opening/closing at any time, was stocked with what we needed so as not to dip into the minbar so often and the man in charge there was always happy to chat. Extremely comfortable beds (we had a tower room) and a more-than adequate bathroom (I have been in 5 stars where the bathroom is smaller). As for the neighborhood - yes it is a bit sleazy but IT IS HOLLYWOOD!!!! You get the same street hassle in any major city. The movies are right across the street (including the must-see Chinese theatre), the tacky museums are also fun to look at (see Hollywood Entertainment Museum, great people there and good value) and the souvenir shops stock a better quality of junk than anywhere else (unlike Venice Beach where every souvenir place is identical) with no hassle to buy stuff, the 101 is very close by and a block behind the Roosevelt is Sunset Boulevard (definitely worth a look). Furthermore, if you want to leave the car behind, then the Metro (across the street) will get you to many places  back for a few dollars (Downtown LA, Chinatown, Universal City, etc). If you are visiting the Hollywood Bowl, the shuttle buses are right across the street at the Highland shopping centre, so you have no tranport worries (we saw REM during our stay). Only irritation we had was the Hi-Speed Internet access required bringing a laptop (not via the TV), although the wonderful internet Cafe a block away called Cyber Java made up for that shortcoming. Also met 2 celebs while staying, and experienced the media circus surrounding the deaths of Johnny Cash and John Ritter - their stars on the walk of fame were close by. Basically, my sympathies to those who had a bad experience, but to those who expected the high society and high class that comes with the 5 star chains, then you should have booked your holiday 70 years ago and you do not have my sympathy at all. Well done all you guys at the Hollywood Roosevelt from a very satisifed customer!!!!!  
<Date>Sep 23, 2003
